Second Argument from Individuation and Its Temporal Generality
Second argument from individuation and its temporal scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument of the deniers that bodies require accidents for individuation, and why it only proves that a body cannot be free from accidents at any time, not that it must have every kind.

Core Idea
Individuation via accidents ensures bodies always need some accident, but not each opposite pair.

This lesson continues with the second argument of the deniers, which appeals to the necessity of individuation. Since bodies are composed of similar atoms (jawahir mutamāthila), their individuation must come from accidents. Without accidents, they would lack individuation. However, the author demonstrates that this argument only establishes that a body must have accidents at all times (pre-eternity and perpetuity), not that it must have one of each pair of opposites for every accident. The lesson also examines the attempt to generalize this argument to all accidents through analogy and the rebuttal that both premises of that generalization are denied.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the key terms 'تشخص', 'جواهر متماثلة', 'غير المتشخص'.
2
Understand the argument from individuation
The argument: a thing cannot exist without individuation; bodies are individuated by accidents because their atoms are similar; without accidents, they would be non-individuated, which is impossible.
This shows that accidents are necessary for the existence of bodies.
3
Distinguish between two types of universality
The author notes the argument does not prove per-accident universality (each opposite pair) but does prove temporal universality (at all times). A single accident suffices for individuation.
Per-accident: must have motion OR stasis for every motion-related accident? No. Temporal: at every time, some accident exists.
4
Examine the generalization via analogy
To extend the argument to all accidents and all times, one would need to analogize pre-eternity to later times and some accidents to others. The proposed premise: the substance's relation to all accidents and times is equal.
5
Learn the refutation
The author answers that both premises of the analogical extension are denied (man‘ al-muqaddimatayn).
This means the generalization fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

How does this reframe your view of your own existence from something self-sufficient to something perpetually dependent? Will you acknowledge that dependency today in a concrete action?

The First Argument: No Compulsion in Creation
First argument and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the inability to bring about a logical impossibility does not detract from God's power or free choice.

Core Idea
Logical impossibility is not a limitation on divine power.

The first argument attempts to show that if bodies necessarily required accidents, God would be forced to create them against His free will. Taftazani responds by distinguishing between true inability and logical impossibility, a crucial distinction in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Identify the claim and the response.
Notice the structure: objection followed by 'الجواب'.
2
Grasp the logical structure
The argument: if body cannot be empty of accident, then God must create accident → compulsion. The response: this is like requiring the existence of a cause without its effect, which is impossible, and inability to do the impossible is not weakness.
Think of 'المحال' as what is inherently impossible.
3
Reflect on the implications
Why does inability to do the impossible not contradict choice? Because choice operates within the realm of possibility; the impossible is outside it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج القائلون بجواز خلو الجسم عن الضدين في الجملة الأول: أنه لو لم يجز لكان الباري تعالى مضطراً عند خلق الجسم إلى خلق العرض، وهو ينافي الاختيار. والجواب : أن عدم القدرة على المحال كوجود الملزوم بدون اللازم لا يوجب العجز وسلب الاختيار. الثاني : أنه لو لم يجز خلو الجسم عن الاجتماع والافتراق لما جاز أن يخلق الله تعالى جسماً هو أول الأجسام بحسب الزمان واللازم قطعى البطلان . الثالث: أنه لو لم يجز خلوه عن جميع الألوان لما وقع وقد وقع كالهواء ، لا يقال : لا نسلّم خلوه عن اللون، بل غايته عدم الإحساس به، لأنـا نقـول عدم الإحساس بما من شأنه الإحساس به مع سلامة الحاسة وسائر الشرائط دليل على عدمه. فإن قيل : من جملة الشرائط انتفاء المانع وتحققه ممنوع . قلنا : فتح هذا الباب يؤدي إلى جواز أن يكون بحضرتنا جبال شامخة، وأصوات هائلة ولا ندركها لمانع . وقد يجاب بأن الشفيف ضد اللون لا عدم.
And those who argued for the permissibility of a body being empty of the two opposites argued in summary with [several] points: First: that if it were not permissible, then the Exalted Creator would be compelled when creating the body to create the accident, and this contradicts choice. The answer: that inability to do the impossible, like the existence of the necessary condition without the necessary consequence, does not necessitate inability and removal of choice. Second: that if it were not permissible for a body to be empty of composition and separation, then it would not be permissible for God the Exalted to create a body that is the first of bodies in time, and the consequent is necessarily false. Third: that if it were not permissible for it to be empty of all colors, then it would not occur, and it has occurred like air. It cannot be said: we do not concede it is empty of color; rather its utmost is the absence of sensing it, because we say: the absence of sensing something that is normally sensed, given the soundness of the sense and all conditions, is evidence of its non-existence. So if it is said: among the conditions is the absence of an obstacle, and its presence is contested. We say: opening this door leads to the permissibility that there be before us lofty mountains and tremendous sounds that we do not perceive due to an obstacle. And it may be answered that transparency is the opposite of color, not non-existence.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments (وجوه) used by those who claim that a body can be empty of both opposites (e.g., color and its absence, composition and separation). The first argument claims that if a body necessarily required an accident upon creation, then God would be compelled to create that accident, which contradicts His voluntary (اختِيار) nature. The author responds (والجواب) that the inability to create the impossible (المحال) – such as the existence of the foundation (ملزوم) without its necessary property (لازم) – does not imply inability (عجز) or removal of choice; it is simply a logical impossibility, not a deficiency. The second argument is stated without an explicit answer here: if a body could not be empty of composition and separation, then God could not create the first body in time (since it would have to have these attributes before anything existed), a self-evident falsity (قطعى البطلان). The third argument uses air as an example of a body that appears colorless; the opponent objects that we do not concede air is truly colorless, but only that we do not sense its color. The author rebuts (لأنا نقول) that the absence of sensation when the sense and conditions are intact proves absence (عدم) of the color. The opponent further objects that one condition is the absence of a hindrance (مانع), which is not proven. The author counters (قلنا) that accepting this would allow absurdities like mountains and sounds present but imperceptible. Finally, an alternative answer is mentioned: transparency (الشفيف) is a color opposite, not the absence of color.

Key Terms
خلو الجسم عن الضدين
العرض
الاختيار
الملزوم
اللازم
المحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's inability to create a body without an accident would be a limitation on His power.
Correction: Inability to do the impossible does not constitute weakness; it is not within the realm of power.

Checkpoint
According to the author's response to the first argument, why does the inability to bring about a necessary conditional without its consequent not contradict God's choice?
A) Because God chooses to create the accident voluntarily.
B) Because the inability to do the impossible does not constitute weakness or remove choice.
C) Because the accident can be created later.
D) Because the body already contains the accident essentially.

Key Takeaway
Inability to do what is logically impossible does not challenge God's omnipotence or free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial that seems impossible to bear, do you secretly believe that God has failed you or is not powerful enough? How does knowing that logical impossibility is not a real limitation on God change the way you view that trial — and what would it take for you to actually surrender it to Him today?
?
You claim to believe that God is free in His actions, but when His commands restrict your desires, do you feel He is taking away your freedom? Use the argument in this lesson: if obeying a necessary command (like prayer) is not compulsion but logical consistency in the created order, what would change if you lived that belief tomorrow?
?
The argument says inability to do the impossible does not negate choice. Think of an area in your life where you feel stuck — a sin pattern or a difficult situation. Are you blaming God for not giving you a way out, when in fact the impossibility is part of your created nature? What would it mean to accept that limitation and turn to Him instead of resenting Him?

Second and Third Arguments: Succession, Color, and Transparency
Second and third arguments for bodies free of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second and third arguments attempt to prove bodies can be free of opposites, and how Taftazani defends this possibility.

Core Idea
Empirical examples like air show that bodies can lack apparent qualities.

The second argument uses the concept of a first body in time, and the third argument uses the example of air being colorless. Taftazani presents these arguments along with a detailed rebuttal to objections about sensory evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the second argument about composition and separation. Why does it claim that if bodies always had these, God could not create the first body?
Notice the argument is presented without an explicit response; the false consequent is stated.
2
Read the third argument and objection
Read the third argument using air as an example. Then read the opponent's objection that we only fail to sense color, not that it is absent.
Pay attention to the back-and-forth: objection, reply, further objection, final reply.
3
Analyze the final answers
Study the two responses: (1) Absence of sensation with intact senses proves absence of the quality, else we could not know anything. (2) Transparency is itself a color, so air does have a color.
The second answer is an alternative, not necessarily endorsed by all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج القائلون بجواز خلو الجسم عن الضدين في الجملة الأول: أنه لو لم يجز لكان الباري تعالى مضطراً عند خلق الجسم إلى خلق العرض، وهو ينافي الاختيار. والجواب : أن عدم القدرة على المحال كوجود الملزوم بدون اللازم لا يوجب العجز وسلب الاختيار. الثاني : أنه لو لم يجز خلو الجسم عن الاجتماع والافتراق لما جاز أن يخلق الله تعالى جسماً هو أول الأجسام بحسب الزمان واللازم قطعى البطلان . الثالث: أنه لو لم يجز خلوه عن جميع الألوان لما وقع وقد وقع كالهواء ، لا يقال : لا نسلّم خلوه عن اللون، بل غايته عدم الإحساس به، لأنـا نقـول عدم الإحساس بما من شأنه الإحساس به مع سلامة الحاسة وسائر الشرائط دليل على عدمه. فإن قيل : من جملة الشرائط انتفاء المانع وتحققه ممنوع . قلنا : فتح هذا الباب يؤدي إلى جواز أن يكون بحضرتنا جبال شامخة، وأصوات هائلة ولا ندركها لمانع . وقد يجاب بأن الشفيف ضد اللون لا عدم.
And those who argued for the permissibility of a body being empty of the two opposites argued in summary with [several] points: First: that if it were not permissible, then the Exalted Creator would be compelled when creating the body to create the accident, and this contradicts choice. The answer: that inability to do the impossible, like the existence of the necessary condition without the necessary consequence, does not necessitate inability and removal of choice. Second: that if it were not permissible for a body to be empty of composition and separation, then it would not be permissible for God the Exalted to create a body that is the first of bodies in time, and the consequent is necessarily false. Third: that if it were not permissible for it to be empty of all colors, then it would not occur, and it has occurred like air. It cannot be said: we do not concede it is empty of color; rather its utmost is the absence of sensing it, because we say: the absence of sensing something that is normally sensed, given the soundness of the sense and all conditions, is evidence of its non-existence. So if it is said: among the conditions is the absence of an obstacle, and its presence is contested. We say: opening this door leads to the permissibility that there be before us lofty mountains and tremendous sounds that we do not perceive due to an obstacle. And it may be answered that transparency is the opposite of color, not non-existence.
Source pages p. 92

The second argument is stated without an explicit answer here: if a body could not be empty of composition and separation, then God could not create the first body in time (since it would have to have these attributes before anything existed), a self-evident falsity (قطعى البطلان). The opponent further objects that one condition is the absence of a hindrance (مانع), which is not proven. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That air is completely colorless and thus proves bodies can be free of all colors.
Correction: Taftazani offers two answers: either air lacks color (proven by sensation) or it has the color of transparency.

Checkpoint
What is the alternative answer given to the third argument regarding air's color?
A) Air is transparent because it has no color.
B) Transparency is a color opposite to opacity.
C) Air has a color that changes with temperature.
D) Air's color is perceived by other senses.

Key Takeaway
The third argument demonstrates that sensory evidence, when properly conditioned, can indicate absence of qualities, but an alternative explanation exists that all bodies have a color.

?
The second argument shows that God's creative power is not bound by the logical constraints we impose on bodies. Think of a situation in your life where you assumed God could not bring about something because it seemed impossible to you. How does this argument challenge you to expand your trust in His power? What concrete step can you take this week to act on that expanded trust?
?
The third argument forces you to rely on sensory evidence under normal conditions, rejecting hypothetical obstacles. In your spiritual life, have you ever allowed hypothetical doubts—'what if there is an unseen obstacle'—to weaken your conviction about a clear truth from revelation? What would it look like for you to close that door and embrace certainty based on the evidence God has given you?
?
The alternate answer that transparency is a color reminds you that what you perceive as absence might actually be a different kind of presence. In your relationship with God, is there an attribute or guidance you have dismissed as 'absent' from your experience, but which might actually be present in a way you have not recognized? How will you actively seek to perceive that presence today?

The Objection Against the First Point of Tangency
Clarifies point's nature and presents objection denying first point.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that denies a necessary first point of tangency due to infinite divisibility and the initial claim that the implication still holds.

Core Idea
Even if distance is infinite, tangency after non-existence implies a first point.

In this lesson, we examine a key objection to the proof requiring a first point of tangency. The objector argues that since motion and angle are infinitely divisible, there can be no first tangency. We'll see the author's initial response that the implication remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the hypothetical point
Read the Arabic passage once, noting how the author clarifies that the point is considered only hypothetically, not as actually existing.
This sets up the conceptual framework for the objection.
2
Identify the objection's reasoning
The objector claims that because motion and angle are infinitely divisible, before every tangency there is another tangency, so no first point exists. Mark the key terms: 'لا تناهي البعد' and 'تنقسمان لا إلى نهاية'.
This is the core of the objection.
3
Note the author's initial response
The author asserts that after arguing that tangency occurred after not existing, it necessarily has a first, so the objection is not valid unless it is made a counterexample in the premise.
This sets up the logical refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا إلى نهاية، والمسامتة بخلافها، وإنما اعتبر النقطة بحسب الوهم، لأن ثبوتها بالفعل غير لازم ما لم ينقطع الخط بالفعل. وفيما أوردنا من تقرير البرهان إشارة إلى دفع اعتراضات تورد عليه فمنها منع لزوم أول نقطة المسامتة مستنداً بما ذكرنا في بيان استحالة اللازم وتقريره أنه على تقدير لا تناهي البعد لا يلزم أول نقطة المسامتة، لأن الحركة والزاوية تنقسمان لا إلى نهاية فقبل كل مسامتة مسامتة لا إلى أول . ولاخفاء في أن هذا بعد الاحتجاج على الملازمة بأن المسامتة حصلت بعدما لم تكن فيكون لها أول بالضرورة ليس بموجه إلا أن تجعل معارضة في المقدمة ، وجوابها النقض بكل قياس استثنائي، استثنى فيه نقيض التالي، فإنه لو صح ما ذكر لصح فيه الاستدلال على نفي الملازمة بما يذكر في بيان استحالة اللازم وفساده بين والحل بأن هذا لا ينفي الملازمة، لأن الملزوم محال فجاز استلزامه للنقيضين مثلاً لو وجد بعد غير متناه مع الفرض المذكور لزم ثبوت أول نقطة المسامتة لما ذكرنا . وعدم ثبوته لما ذكرتم على أنه يتجه أن يقال لو وجد البعد مع الفرض المذكور، فإما أن تثبت أول نقطة المسامتة أو لا تثبت ، وكلاهما محال ، لما ذكر فيتم الاحتجاج .
Not [continuing] to infinity, and tangency is contrary to it, and the point is considered only hypothetically, because its actual existence is not necessary unless the line is actually cut. And in what we have presented of the formulation of the proof is an indication of repelling objections that are brought against it. Among them is the denial of the necessity of the first point of tangency, relying on what we mentioned in the explanation of the impossibility of the consequent and its formulation: that given the assumption of infinite distance, the first point of tangency does not necessarily follow, because motion and angle are infinitely divisible, so before every tangency there is a tangency without a first. And it is clear that this, after arguing for the implication that the tangency occurred after not being, so it necessarily has a first, is not a valid refutation unless it is made as a counterargument in the premise. And its answer is a counterexample with every exceptional syllogism (qiyās istithnāʾī) in which the contradictory of the consequent is assumed, because if what he mentioned were correct, then it would be valid to infer the negation of the implication by what is mentioned in the explanation of the impossibility of the consequent, and its falsity is obvious. And the solution is that this does not negate the implication, because the antecedent is impossible, so it is permissible for it to entail contradictories. For example, if an infinite distance existed with the mentioned assumption, then the first point of tangency would necessarily be established for the reason we mentioned, and its non-establishment for the reason you mentioned. However, it is appropriate to say: if the distance existed with the mentioned assumption, then either the first point of tangency is established or not, and both are impossible, for the reason mentioned, so the argument is completed.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-response unit within a larger kalam argument about the impossibility of an infinite regress. The author, al-Taftazani, is defending a proof (burhān) that requires a first point of tangency (musāmatah). He begins by clarifying that the point is considered only hypothetically (bi-ḥasab al-wahm), not actually existing. Then he mentions that the proof includes a refutation of objections. The first objection denies the necessity of a first point of tangency, arguing that since motion and angle are infinitely divisible, there can always be a prior tangency. The author responds by noting that this objection fails to undermine the implication (mulāzamah) because the premise that tangency occurred after not existing logically implies a first. The objection can only be a counterexample in the premise. He then uses the logic of the exceptional syllogism (qiyās istithnāʾī) to show that if the objection were valid, it would allow negation of implication based on the impossibility of the consequent, which is false. The true solution is that the impossibility of the consequent does not negate the implication if the antecedent is itself impossible; an impossible antecedent can entail contradictions. He gives an example: if an infinite distance existed with the assumption, both the establishment and non-establishment of the first point would be impossible, so the argument stands.

Key Terms
مسامتة
البرهان
الملازمة
لا تناهي البعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite divisibility of motion and angle necessarily negates the existence of a first point of tangency.
Correction: The author argues that tangency occurring after non-existence logically requires a first point, regardless of infinite divisibility; the objection fails unless it is a counterexample in the premise.

Checkpoint
Why does the author initially reject the objection from infinite divisibility?
A) Because the point is actual, not hypothetical.
B) Because tangency occurred after not existing, so it must have a first.
C) Because infinite distance is impossible.
D) Because the objection relies on a false premise.

Key Takeaway
The objection from infinite divisibility does not invalidate the implication because the occurrence of tangency after non-existence logically requires a first.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone raises an objection that seems to undermine a truth you hold, do you instinctively dismiss it or do you carefully examine whether the objection actually targets your premise? This lesson challenges you to defend your beliefs with precision. Will you commit to studying the logical structure of your faith so that you are not swayed by clever but invalid objections?
?
The author treats the point as hypothetical, yet maintains its logical implication. Are there aspects of your faith that you treat as merely theoretical, not allowing them to demand real change in your actions? What is one truth you have been avoiding living out, and what step will you take today to move from theoretical acceptance to actual submission?
?
The objector uses infinite divisibility to deny a first point, but the author insists the implication holds. Is there a sin or habit in your life that you justify by appealing to complexity or gradual change, convincing yourself there is no 'first point' of repentance? This lesson says that when something begins, there must be a first. When will you take that first step to turn back to Allah?

Refuting the Objection Through Logical Analysis
Al-Taftazani refutes objection using exceptional syllogism and impossible antecedent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani uses the exceptional syllogism (qiyās istithnāʾī) to refute the objection and shows that an impossible antecedent can entail contradictories.

Core Idea
An impossible antecedent does not negate the implication; it can even entail both sides of a contradiction.

In this second part, al-Taftazani deepens the refutation by applying the logic of exceptional syllogisms. He demonstrates that the objection's reasoning would undermine all syllogisms of this type, and then provides the true solution: the impossibility of the antecedent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the exceptional syllogism
Read the passage and note the structure of qiyās istithnāʾī, where the contradictory of the consequent is assumed. The author uses this to counter the objection.
Familiarize yourself with the logic: if the antecedent implies the consequent, denying the consequent leads to denying the antecedent.
2
See how the objection would be a counterexample
The objection's reasoning would apply to any such syllogism, allowing denial of the implication based on the impossibility of the consequent. The author points out this is false.
This shows the objection's logic is too broad.
3
Grasp the true solution
The true solution is that the impossibility of the consequent does not negate the implication because the antecedent itself is impossible. An impossible antecedent can entail both a thing and its negation.
Example: if infinite distance existed, both establishment and non-establishment of the first point would be impossible.
4
Complete the argument
The author concludes that since both possibilities lead to impossibility, the original proof stands.
This reinforces the necessity of a first point under correct assumptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا إلى نهاية، والمسامتة بخلافها، وإنما اعتبر النقطة بحسب الوهم، لأن ثبوتها بالفعل غير لازم ما لم ينقطع الخط بالفعل. وفيما أوردنا من تقرير البرهان إشارة إلى دفع اعتراضات تورد عليه فمنها منع لزوم أول نقطة المسامتة مستنداً بما ذكرنا في بيان استحالة اللازم وتقريره أنه على تقدير لا تناهي البعد لا يلزم أول نقطة المسامتة، لأن الحركة والزاوية تنقسمان لا إلى نهاية فقبل كل مسامتة مسامتة لا إلى أول . ولاخفاء في أن هذا بعد الاحتجاج على الملازمة بأن المسامتة حصلت بعدما لم تكن فيكون لها أول بالضرورة ليس بموجه إلا أن تجعل معارضة في المقدمة ، وجوابها النقض بكل قياس استثنائي، استثنى فيه نقيض التالي، فإنه لو صح ما ذكر لصح فيه الاستدلال على نفي الملازمة بما يذكر في بيان استحالة اللازم وفساده بين والحل بأن هذا لا ينفي الملازمة، لأن الملزوم محال فجاز استلزامه للنقيضين مثلاً لو وجد بعد غير متناه مع الفرض المذكور لزم ثبوت أول نقطة المسامتة لما ذكرنا . وعدم ثبوته لما ذكرتم على أنه يتجه أن يقال لو وجد البعد مع الفرض المذكور، فإما أن تثبت أول نقطة المسامتة أو لا تثبت ، وكلاهما محال ، لما ذكر فيتم الاحتجاج .

القياس الاستثنائي
نقيض التالي
الملازمة
الملزوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the consequent of an implication is impossible, then the implication is false.
Correction: The implication can still hold if the antecedent is impossible; an impossible antecedent can entail anything, including contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the true solution to the objection?
A) The objection is valid and disproves the proof.
B) The implication is negated because the consequent is impossible.
C) The implication holds because the antecedent is impossible, and can entail contradictories.
D) The objection is answered by showing that motion is finite.

Key Takeaway
The objection fails because the antecedent is impossible, and an impossible antecedent can entail contradictions without breaking the implication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a contradiction in your understanding of a matter of faith, do you immediately assume the belief is false, or do you examine whether your underlying assumption might be impossible? This lesson shows that an impossible antecedent can lead to contradictions without falsifying the implication. Take a moment to identify one doubt you have struggled with and ask yourself: what is the 'antecedent' assumption I am making? Is it impossible?
?
The author uses rigorous logic to defend a theological truth. In your own life, do you rely on careful reasoning or emotional reactions when facing objections to your faith? Commit to studying the logical foundations of one core belief this week, not just relying on feelings.
?
If the implication (al-mulāzama) between your actions and your faith's promises were valid, but your own 'antecedent' (your current state) were impossible due to sin, would you despair? Or would you realize that an impossible antecedent does not break the implication, but calls you to change the antecedent? How does this affect your view of repentance?

The Necessity of a Spatial First Point of Tangency
Al-Taftazani answers an objection by linking time, motion, and distance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the occurrence of tangency requires a spatial first point, not just a temporal beginning, through the mapping of time onto motion onto distance.

Core Idea
Time, motion, and distance are layered: no first point in distance means no first in motion or time.

In the ongoing discussion about tangency and temporal beginnings, an objector raises a subtle point: even if tangency occurs, why must it have a spatial starting point? Al-Taftazani responds by revealing the necessary link between time, motion, and distance. This short but powerful argument shows that the very structure of motion and time depends on spatial boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector claims that the occurrence of tangency only implies a beginning in time, not necessarily a first point in space. Understand the distinction being made.
The objector is not denying temporal beginning; they are questioning the necessity of a spatial one.
2
Examine the response
Al-Taftazani's answer uses the concept of 'inṭibāq' (superimposition): time is superimposed onto motion, and motion onto distance. This means that if distance had no first point, motion would have no first, and consequently time would have no first.
This is a logical argument, not an empirical one.
3
Reflect on the implication
The absurdity of time having no first is taken as a reductio ad absurdum. Therefore, the spatial first point is necessary. Ask yourself: why does time having no first matter in this context?
The argument relies on the assumption that time began—a key tenet in kalam cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: حدوث المسامتة لا يقتضي إلا أن لها بداية بحسب الزمان، فمن أين تلزم البداية بحسب المسافة، أعني أول نقطة المسامتة.؟ قلنا: من جهة أن الزمان منطبق على الحركة المنطبقة على المسافة، فلو لم يكن لها أول لم يكن للحركة أول، فلم يكن للزمان أول،
For if it is said: The occurrence of tangency does not imply except that it has a beginning in terms of time; so from where is a beginning in terms of distance, i.e., the first point of tangency, necessitated? We say: Because time is superimposed onto motion which is superimposed onto distance, so if it had no first, then motion would have no first, and then time would have no first.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objector argues that the occurrence (ḥudūth) of tangency only requires a beginning in time, not necessarily a first spatial point along the distance. The author responds by stating that time maps onto motion (ḥarakah), which in turn maps onto distance (masāfah). Therefore, if the spatial tangency had no first point, the motion would have no first, and consequently time would have no first—which is absurd. Thus, the spatial beginning is necessary.

Key Terms
حدوث (ḥudūth)
المسامتة (musāmatah)
الزمان (al-zamān)
المسافة (al-masāfah)
انطباق (inṭibāq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that temporal beginning does not imply spatial beginning, and thus tangency could begin without a first spatial point.
Correction: Al-Taftazani shows that because time, motion, and distance are co-extensive (time superimposed on motion superimposed on distance), the absence of a spatial first point would lead to the absence of a first moment of motion and time, contradicting the fact that time has a beginning.

Checkpoint
How does the author argue that a spatial first point of tangency is necessary?
A) By citing a religious text.
B) By showing that time, motion, and distance are co-extensive.
C) By denying the possibility of infinite time.
D) By appealing to divine power.

Key Takeaway
The spatial first point of tangency is necessary because time, motion, and distance are inseparably linked through superimposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider that Al-Taftazani argues time, motion, and distance are inseparably linked: if one lacks a beginning, the others do too. In your own life, have you ever separated your actions (motion) from their consequences over time, thinking that a small beginning doesn't matter? How does this layered argument challenge you to see that every small starting point – a word, a thought, a decision – has an impact that reaches through time and space? What first step have you been avoiding because you didn't see its necessity?
?
The objector thought a temporal beginning doesn't imply a spatial beginning. You might similarly separate your external actions from your internal state, thinking that outward obedience doesn't require inward transformation. But Al-Taftazani’s insistence on the connection between layers reveals that Allah’s creation has no such disconnection. Where in your life are you living as though your heart can have no 'first point' of change while your actions have a beginning? What would it mean for you to seek a true first step inside yourself?
?
If time, motion, and distance are superimposed by Allah's design, then nothing in your experience is random – every moment, movement, and place is precisely ordered and accounted for. Does your daily schedule reflect this belief? If you truly lived as though every second and every inch of your day has a purpose set by Allah, what would you change about your morning, your work, your interactions? Refuting the Objection: Impossibility from the Combination
Al-Taftazani refutes the objection that impossibility is from the combination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani refutes the claim that the impossibility stems from the combination of infinite distance with a supposition, not from the infinite distance itself.

Core Idea
Infinite distance is the real cause of impossibility, not the combination.

This passage presents a crucial objection and its refutation. The objector argues that the impossibility in the argument arises from combining infinite distance with a specific supposition, rather than from the infinite distance itself. Al-Taftazani responds by appealing to necessary knowledge: since the supposition is possible on its own and can combine with infinite distance, the impossibility must be caused by the infinite distance alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Start by reading the objection: 'If it is said: The impossibility only follows given the assumption of infinite distance with the mentioned supposition...' Understand the objector's claim that the impossibility might be due to the combination.
2
Identify the objector's reasoning
The objector says the impossibility does not prove infinite distance is impossible per se, because it could arise from the combination. Grasp this shift of blame.
3
Read al-Taftazani's response
Read the answer: 'We know by necessity the possibility of what was supposed, and the possibility of its combination with infinite distance, so it is determined that the infinite distance is the source.' Note the use of 'by necessity' (bi-l-ḍarūrah).
4
Analyze the logic
If the supposition by itself is possible, and the combination is also possible, then the impossibility when combined must come from the infinite distance. This refutes the objection.
5
Conclude the lesson
Conclude that infinite distance is impossible because it alone causes the contradiction. This is a foundational move in the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: المحال إنما لزم على تقدير لا تناهي البعد مع الفرض المذكور وهو لا يستلزم استحالة لا تناهي البعد لجواز أن يكون ناشئاً من المجموع . وجوابه: أنا نعلم بالضرورة إمكان ما فرض، وإمكان اجتماعه مع البعد الغير المتناهي، فتعين كونه المنشأ للزوم المحال
For if it is said: The impossibility only follows given the assumption of infinite distance with the mentioned supposition, and it does not entail the impossibility of infinite distance because it may arise from the combination. And its answer: We know by necessity the possibility of what was supposed, and the possibility of its combination with infinite distance, so it is determined that the infinite distance is the source of the necessary impossibility.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This is another objection and answer. The objector argues that the impossibility (muḥāl) that arises in the argument is not due to the infinite distance itself but rather due to the combination of the infinite distance with the assumed motion or tangency. Therefore, it does not prove that infinite distance is impossible per se. The author responds that we know by necessity (bi-l-ḍarūrah) that the assumed supposition (e.g., a rotating sphere) is possible, and it is also possible for it to be combined with an infinite distance. Since the impossibility arises only when combined with infinite distance, the infinite distance must be the cause of the impossibility. Thus, infinite distance is impossible.

Key Terms
المحال (al-muḥāl)
تقدير (taqdīr)
المجموع (al-majmūʿ)
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the impossibility could be due to the combination, not the infinite distance itself.
Correction: Al-Taftazani argues that since the supposition is possible on its own and can combine with infinite distance, the impossibility when combined must be caused by the infinite distance.

Checkpoint
Why does the author conclude that infinite distance is impossible?
A) Because any combination with it is impossible.
B) Because the assumed supposition is possible and its combination with infinite distance leads to impossibility, so the infinite distance is the cause.
C) Because infinite distance is logically contradictory.
D) Because the objector concedes that it is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Infinite distance is impossible because it alone causes the impossibility in the argument, not the combination with a possible supposition.

Do you live as if you know certain truths about Allah and His creation by necessity, or do you let intellectual complacency leave room for unnecessary doubts? Commit to acting this week on one necessary truth about Allah's oneness, as if you could not doubt it.

Burhan al-Tatbiq: The Proof of Application for Finitude
Presents and explains the proof of application for finitude of dimensions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of Burhan al-Tatbiq and why it demonstrates that dimensions cannot be infinite.

Core Idea
An infinite dimension cannot exist because comparing it with its part leads to contradiction.

In this passage, the author presents the third proof for the finitude of dimensions, known as the Proof of Application (Burhan al-Tatbiq). This proof uses a simple thought experiment: subtract one cubit from an infinite dimension and mentally overlay the remainder. The contradiction that arises shows that the original dimension must be finite. Let's examine the reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage carefully. Notice how the author starts by stating the proof's procedure.
Pay attention to the two possibilities presented.
2
Understand the two possibilities
The proof presents two possible outcomes of applying the deficient dimension onto the complete. Identify them and understand why the first is impossible.
The first possibility implies equality of whole and part, which is absurd.
3
Trace the conclusion
See how the second possibility leads to the termination of the deficient dimension, and then the complete dimension must also terminate because it is only one cubit longer.
This contradicts the assumption of an infinite dimension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الثالث إنا أن ننقص من البعد الغير المتناهي ذراعاً نطبق، فإما أن يقع بإزاء كل ذراع ذراع فيتساوان، أو لا فينقطعان، وقد مر مثله، وهذه الثلاثة هي الأصول في براهين التناهي. هذا برهان التطبيق، وتقريره أنه لو وجد بعد غير متناه، نفرض نقصان ذراع منه، ثم نطبق بين البعد التام والناقص، فإما أن يقع بإزاء كل ذراع من التام ذراع من الناقص، وهو محال لامتناع تساوي الزائد والناقص، بل الكل والجزء، أو لا يقع ولا محالة يكون ذلك بانقطاع الناقص، ويلزم منه انقطاع التام لأنه لا يزيد عليه إلا بذراع، وقد مرّ في إبطال التسلسل ما على هذا البرهان من الاعتراضات والأجوبة فلا معنى للإعادة .
He said (the third): If we subtract a cubit from an infinite dimension and then apply (the remainder), then either every cubit of the original will be opposite a cubit of the remainder, so they are equal, or not, so one terminates; and similar has passed. These three are the principles in the proofs of finitude. This is the proof of application (burhan al-tatbiq). Its exposition: If there existed an infinite dimension, we suppose subtracting a cubit from it, then we apply between the complete dimension and the deficient. Then either every cubit of the complete is opposite a cubit of the deficient, which is impossible because equality of the greater and the lesser—rather whole and part—is impossible; or not, and inevitably that occurs by the deficient terminating, from which follows the termination of the complete because it exceeds it only by a cubit. And there have passed in the refutation of regress (ibṭāl al-tasalsul) the objections and answers against this proof, so there is no need for repetition.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof for the finitude of dimensions, known as burhan al-tatbiq (proof of application). The author begins by stating the proof: assume an infinite dimension, subtract one cubit from it, then mentally overlay the remainder onto the original. Two possibilities arise: either each cubit of the original corresponds to a cubit of the remainder, implying equality between the whole and its part—which is impossible; or there is no such correspondence, in which case the remainder must terminate at some point, and since the whole is only one cubit longer, it too must terminate. Thus, the assumption of an infinite dimension leads to a contradiction. The author then notes that the objections and responses to this proof were already covered in the section on refuting regress (ibṭāl al-tasalsul), so they are not repeated here. This proof relies on the impossibility of comparing an infinite magnitude with its part.

Key Terms
برهان التطبيق
بعد غير متناه
ذراع
إبطال التسلسل
تناهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of application relies on physically superimposing one dimension onto another.
Correction: The proof uses mental application (tatbiq) assumed possible by the opponent; it does not require actual physical superposition.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the proof of application (burhan al-tatbiq)?
A) Infinite dimensions are possible.
B) Infinite dimensions must terminate.
C) The whole equals its part.
D) The proof is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Proof of Application demonstrates that assuming an infinite dimension leads to logical contradiction, thereby proving that all dimensions are finite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that the universe cannot be infinite—it must be finite and thus created. If your life is a finite gift from an eternal Creator, what are you doing today that reflects that reality? Will you spend your next hour pursuing what truly matters?
?
The proof forces you to accept a logical conclusion even when your senses cannot perceive the infinite. In what area of your faith are you relying on your limited perception rather than the clear proofs of revelation and reason? What step will you take this week to submit your assumptions to truth?
?
If time itself is finite, then every moment is precious and irreplaceable. What are you procrastinating that you know you should do for your Creator? Commit now to one specific action you will take before the end of today.

Foundations of the Three Proofs for Finitude
Analyzes the metaphysical basis of the three proofs for finitude of dimensions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct metaphysical assumptions underlying each of the three proofs for the finitude of dimensions.

Core Idea
The three proofs for finitude rest on distinct metaphysical commitments.

In this passage, the author lays out the foundational premises of the three main proofs used by kalam theologians to argue for the finitude of dimensions. Each proof relies on a specific metaphysical commitment—rejection of the indivisible atom, assumption of infinite extension in all directions, or weak premises from the refutation of regress. Understanding these foundations is crucial because the strength or weakness of each proof depends on the plausibility of its starting assumptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice that the author lists three proofs and briefly states their foundations.
The proofs are: burhan al-musamata, burhan al-sullami, and burhan al-tatbiq.
2
Identify each proof's foundation
For each proof, identify the key premise mentioned. The first proof denies the indivisible atom; the second assumes infinity in all directions; the third relies on several weak premises.
Look for phrases like 'نفي الجزء' and 'مقدمات واهية'.
3
Understand the terminology
Familiarize yourself with the technical terms: al-jawhar al-fard (indivisible atom), wahm (estimation), and the names of the proofs.
These terms recur in kalam discussions of finitude.
4
Reflect on the author's evaluation
Note that the author calls the third proof's premises 'weak'. Consider why this might be and how it affects the proof's reliability.
This connects to the broader debate about which proof is most robust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومبنى الأول على نفي الجزء، والثاني على أن يكون اللاتناهي من جهات، والثالث على مقدمات واهية. أي برهان المسامتة على نفي الجوهر الفرد ليصح انقسام الحركة والزاوية إلى غير النهاية، ومبنى البرهان السلمي على أن يكون لا تناهي البعد من جهات حتى نفرض انفراج ساقي المثلث لا إلى نهاية بل في الترسى لا بد من فرض اللا تناهي في جميع الجهات وكان طرق السلمى مبنية على طريق إلزام القائلين بلا تناهي الأبعاد في جميع الجهات، ومبنى برهان التطبيق على مقدمات ضعيفة سبقت الإشارة إليها في إبطال التسلسل مثل اقتدار الوهم على التطبيق، ومثل استلزام وقوع ذراع بإزاء ذراع للتساوي، ومثل اختصاص ذلك بما له وضع وترتيب ليحصل التقصي عن النقض بمراتب الأعداد، وحركات الأفلاك.
He said: The basis of the first is the denial of the part (indivisible atom), the second that infinity is from directions, and the third on weak premises. That is, the proof of parallelism (burhan al-musamata) is based on denying the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) so that the division of motion and angle ad infinitum is correct. The basis of the ladder proof (al-burhan al-sullami) is that the infinity of dimension is from directions, so that we suppose the divergence of the sides of the triangle ad infinitum, but in the ladder one must suppose infinity in all directions. And the way of the ladder proof is based on compelling those who affirm infinite dimensions in all directions. And the basis of the proof of application is on weak premises previously indicated in the refutation of regress, such as the ability of the estimation (wahm) to apply, and such as the entailment of a cubit opposite a cubit for equality, and such as its restriction to that which has position and order to achieve avoidance of refutation by the ranks of numbers and the motions of the spheres.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage explains the foundations (mabāni) of the three proofs for the finitude of dimensions. The first proof (burhan al-musamata, proof of parallelism) is based on rejecting the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), which allows motion and angles to be infinitely divisible. The second proof (al-burhan al-sullami, ladder proof) assumes that infinity extends in all directions, such that the sides of a triangle diverge infinitely and the ladder must also be infinite. Its method is to compel those who accept infinite dimensions in all directions. The third proof (burhan al-tatbiq) is built on weak premises previously discussed in the refutation of regress, specifically: (1) the ability of the estimation (wahm) to perform the mental application, (2) the assumption that a one-to-one correspondence of cubits entails equality, and (3) the restriction of this correspondence to things with position and order to avoid counterexamples from numbers and celestial motions.

Key Terms
الجوهر الفرد
برهان المسامتة
برهان السلمي
برهان التطبيق
وهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All three proofs for finitude are equally strong and based on similar metaphysical assumptions.
Correction: Each proof rests on different foundations, and the author explicitly states that the third proof's premises are weak, distinguishing it from the others.

Checkpoint
Which proof is based on the denial of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard)?
A) Burhan al-tatbiq
B) Burhan al-musamata
C) Al-burhan al-sullami
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The three proofs for finitude of dimensions are built on very different metaphysical premises, ranging from the denial of the indivisible atom to weak assumptions about mental correspondence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that the third proof relies on weak premises. Are you willing to critically examine the foundations of your own beliefs, even if they seem well-established? What would it take for you to abandon a weak argument you have trusted?
?
The first proof requires denying the indivisible atom. Do you have any assumptions that you hold as 'indivisible'—unquestionable? Is your faith stronger when it rests on firm metaphysical grounds or on unquestioned assumptions?
?
The author exposes the weak premises of one proof while accepting others. Do you examine the foundations of your own knowledge of God and creation, or do you accept proofs because they are traditional? Challenge yourself: which of your beliefs about God's attributes rests on solid reasoning, and which on weak premises?

Proof of Escape (Burhan al-Takhallus) and the Objection
Taftazani presents the takhallus proof, objection, and response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the proof of escape demonstrates the impossibility of infinite dimensions and why the objection regarding the movement of an infinite line is misguided.

Core Idea
Infinite lines cannot 'escape' each other because they have no endpoint.

This lesson examines the first of two proofs against infinite dimensions. The proof imagines two infinite lines and a rotating sphere to derive a contradiction. An important objection is addressed, clarifying that the proof only requires the finite diameter to move, not the infinite line itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for context
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the proof begins with the assumption that infinite dimensions are possible.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the setup
Identify the components: a sphere with an infinite radius intersecting another infinite line, then the sphere rotates.
3
Follow the contradiction
The radius must go from intersecting to tangent to parallel. This requires one line to 'escape' the other at a point, but infinite lines have no such point.
The contradiction is that the escape is impossible.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The objection denies that an infinite line can move. The response clarifies that only the finite diameter moves, so the objection is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ببراهين إبطال التسلسل، أما وجوه التصرف في السلمى، فقد سبقت وأما في المسامتة فوجهان : أحدهما: برهان التخلص وتقريره أنه لو أمكن لا تناهي الأبعاد لأمكن أن نفرض كرة يخرج من مركزها خط غير متناه ملازم له مقاطع لخط آخر غير متناه، وأن تتحرك تلك الكرة على نفسها، فبالضرورة يصير الخط الخارج من مركزها بعد المقاطعة مسامتاً ثم موازياً، لكن ذلك محال لتوقفه على تخلص أحد الخطين عن الآخر وهو يتصور إلا بنقطة هي - من أحد الخطين، وقد فرضناهما غير متناهيين هذا خلف ويرد عليه منع إمكان حركة الخط الغير المتناهي سيما بحيث ينتهي من المقاطعة إلى المسامتة إلى الموازاة. وأورد أبو البركات هذا المنع على برهان المسامتة وتبعه صاحب الإشراق في المطارحات، ولا يظهر له وجه، لأن المفروض هناك حركة قطر الكرة وهو متناه . لا هي [؟] وثانيهما: برهان الموازاة وهو أن نفرض قطر الكرة مسامتاً للخط الغير المتناهي، ثم موازياً له بحركة الكرة فلانتهاء المسامتة يلزم في الخط الغير المتناهي نقطة آخر نقطة المسامتة وهو محال، لأن كل نقطة تفرض كذلك. فالمسامتة بما فوقها بعد المسامتة بها
From the proofs of the impossibility of infinite regression. As for the aspects of handling in the ladder [sulmi?] they have preceded. And as for tangency [musamata] there are two aspects: One of them: the proof of escape [takhallus] and its formulation is that if infinite dimensions were possible, then it would be possible for us to assume a sphere from whose center extends an infinite line contiguous with it intersecting another infinite line, and that sphere rotates on itself, then necessarily the line extending from its center after intersection becomes tangential then parallel. But this is impossible because it depends on one of the two lines escaping from the other, and this is conceivable only by a point that is from one of the two lines, and we have assumed them to be infinite. This is a contradiction. And it is rebutted by denying the possibility of the movement of the infinite line, especially such that it ends from intersection to tangency to parallelism. And Abu al-Barakat raised this objection against the proof of musamata, and was followed by the author of al-Ishraq in al-Mutarahat, but there is no basis for it, because what is assumed there is the movement of the diameter of the sphere, which is finite. [unclear] And the second is the proof of parallelism [muwazat]: that we assume the diameter of the sphere tangential to the infinite line, then parallel to it by the rotation of the sphere. So due to the finitude of the tangency, there would necessarily be in the infinite line a point that is the last point of tangency, which is absurd because every point is assumed similarly. So the tangency beyond it is after the tangency with it.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs against the possibility of infinite dimensions, both based on the concept of tangency (musamata). The first proof is called the 'proof of escape' (burhan al-takhallus). It imagines a sphere with a radius that is an infinite line intersecting another infinite line. If the sphere rotates, the radius would go from intersecting to being tangent and then parallel to the other line. This requires the radius to 'escape' from the other line at some point, but since both lines are infinite, there is no such point—leading to a contradiction. An objection is raised that an infinite line cannot rotate, but the author notes this objection misunderstands the proof because the movement is of the sphere's diameter, which is finite. The second proof is the 'proof of parallelism' (burhan al-muwazat). Here, the sphere's diameter is initially tangent to an infinite line, then becomes parallel through rotation. For the tangency to end, there must be a last point of tangency on the infinite line, but since the line is infinite and homogeneous, any assumed last point would imply another point beyond it—an absurdity. Both proofs demonstrate that infinite extension leads to impossible consequences.

Key Terms
برهان التخلص (burhan al-takhallus)
المسامتة (al-musamata)
غير متناه (ghayr mutanahi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof requires an infinite line to move, which is impossible.
Correction: The movement is of the sphere's diameter, which is finite; the infinite line is assumed stationary.

Checkpoint
What is the key contradiction in the takhallus proof?
A) The sphere cannot rotate if its radius is infinite.
B) The two infinite lines cannot intersect.
C) Escape requires a last point of contact, but infinite lines have no endpoint.
D) The diameter of the sphere is infinite.

Key Takeaway
The takhallus proof shows that infinite dimensions lead to a contradiction because lines cannot 'escape' without an endpoint.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that an 'escape' from accountability requires an endpoint—a last point of contact. In your life, are you trying to 'escape' from something you know is true about Allah or yourself, hoping it will go on without resolution? Will you stop avoiding and face that endpoint today?
?
The objection in the passage was dismissed because it misunderstood what was moving. Are there objections you hold against Islamic teachings that are based on a misunderstanding of what is actually being claimed? What would it take for you to re-examine that objection with the same precision as Taftazani?
?
The proof begins by assuming infinite dimensions just to show their impossibility. Have you ever entertained assumptions about your own existence—like thinking your deeds have no ultimate consequence—that you have not seriously tested? What would change if you subjected that assumption to a similar logical scrutiny?

Proof of Parallelism (Burhan al-Muwazat)
Taftazani presents the muwazat proof against infinite dimensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the proof of parallelism demonstrates the impossibility of infinite dimensions by showing that an infinite line cannot have a last point of tangency.

Core Idea
Tangency on an infinite line cannot end, because there is no last point.

This lesson covers the second proof against infinite dimensions: the proof of parallelism. It uses a rotating sphere whose diameter goes from tangent to parallel to an infinite line. The proof shows that if tangency ends, the infinite line must have a last point of tangency, which is absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the setup: the sphere's diameter is initially tangent to an infinite line, then becomes parallel.
2
Identify the key implication
For tangency to end, there must be a last point of tangency on the infinite line.
Think about what it means for a finite segment to end on an infinite line.
3
Recognize the absurdity
Every point on the infinite line is similar; if one is the last, another beyond it could be assumed, leading to contradiction.
4
Connect to impossibility
Since the assumption of infinite dimensions requires this absurd last point, infinite dimensions are impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ببراهين إبطال التسلسل، أما وجوه التصرف في السلمى، فقد سبقت وأما في المسامتة فوجهان : أحدهما: برهان التخلص وتقريره أنه لو أمكن لا تناهي الأبعاد لأمكن أن نفرض كرة يخرج من مركزها خط غير متناه ملازم له مقاطع لخط آخر غير متناه، وأن تتحرك تلك الكرة على نفسها، فبالضرورة يصير الخط الخارج من مركزها بعد المقاطعة مسامتاً ثم موازياً، لكن ذلك محال لتوقفه على تخلص أحد الخطين عن الآخر وهو يتصور إلا بنقطة هي - من أحد الخطين، وقد فرضناهما غير متناهيين هذا خلف ويرد عليه منع إمكان حركة الخط الغير المتناهي سيما بحيث ينتهي من المقاطعة إلى المسامتة إلى الموازاة. وأورد أبو البركات هذا المنع على برهان المسامتة وتبعه صاحب الإشراق في المطارحات، ولا يظهر له وجه، لأن المفروض هناك حركة قطر الكرة وهو متناه . لا هي [؟] وثانيهما: برهان الموازاة وهو أن نفرض قطر الكرة مسامتاً للخط الغير المتناهي، ثم موازياً له بحركة الكرة فلانتهاء المسامتة يلزم في الخط الغير المتناهي نقطة آخر نقطة المسامتة وهو محال، لأن كل نقطة تفرض كذلك. فالمسامتة بما فوقها بعد المسامتة بها
From the proofs of the impossibility of infinite regression. As for the aspects of handling in the ladder [sulmi?] they have preceded. And as for tangency [musamata] there are two aspects: One of them: the proof of escape [takhallus] and its formulation is that if infinite dimensions were possible, then it would be possible for us to assume a sphere from whose center extends an infinite line contiguous with it intersecting another infinite line, and that sphere rotates on itself, then necessarily the line extending from its center after intersection becomes tangential then parallel. But this is impossible because it depends on one of the two lines escaping from the other, and this is conceivable only by a point that is from one of the two lines, and we have assumed them to be infinite. This is a contradiction. And it is rebutted by denying the possibility of the movement of the infinite line, especially such that it ends from intersection to tangency to parallelism. And Abu al-Barakat raised this objection against the proof of musamata, and was followed by the author of al-Ishraq in al-Mutarahat, but there is no basis for it, because what is assumed there is the movement of the diameter of the sphere, which is finite. [unclear] And the second is the proof of parallelism [muwazat]: that we assume the diameter of the sphere tangential to the infinite line, then parallel to it by the rotation of the sphere. So due to the finitude of the tangency, there would necessarily be in the infinite line a point that is the last point of tangency, which is absurd because every point is assumed similarly. So the tangency beyond it is after the tangency with it.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs against the possibility of infinite dimensions, both based on the concept of tangency (musamata). The first proof is called the 'proof of escape' (burhan al-takhallus). It imagines a sphere with a radius that is an infinite line intersecting another infinite line. If the sphere rotates, the radius would go from intersecting to being tangent and then parallel to the other line. This requires the radius to 'escape' from the other line at some point, but since both lines are infinite, there is no such point—leading to a contradiction. An objection is raised that an infinite line cannot rotate, but the author notes this objection misunderstands the proof because the movement is of the sphere's diameter, which is finite. The second proof is the 'proof of parallelism' (burhan al-muwazat). Here, the sphere's diameter is initially tangent to an infinite line, then becomes parallel through rotation. For the tangency to end, there must be a last point of tangency on the infinite line, but since the line is infinite and homogeneous, any assumed last point would imply another point beyond it—an absurdity. Both proofs demonstrate that infinite extension leads to impossible consequences.

Key Terms
برهان الموازاة (burhan al-muwazat)
المسامتة (al-musamata)
الخط غير المتناهي (al-khatt ghayr al-mutanahi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite line can have a last point because the tangency ends at some location.
Correction: An infinite line is endless; no point can be the last because there is always another point beyond.

Checkpoint
Why is the existence of a last point of tangency impossible on an infinite line?
A) The infinite line is too long.
B) Every point on an infinite line is assumed to be similar, so no point can be the last.
C) The sphere's diameter is infinite.
D) Tangency cannot end.

Key Takeaway
The muwazat proof shows that infinite dimensions are impossible because an infinite line cannot have a last point of tangency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof forces you to accept that the universe cannot be infinite. If the universe had a beginning, then you too had a beginning. Does your daily life reflect the reality that you are a created being with a limited time, or do you live as if you will never die? What one concrete change can you make today to live with the urgency of the Hereafter?
?
The proof shows that an infinite series of events backwards is impossible. That means your existence is not the result of an endless chain of causes—it ultimately depends on a Necessary Being. Are you truly living in recognition that Allah is the only independent reality, or do you rely on created things as if they were self-sufficient?
?
The muwazat argument humbles the intellect: it proves something about reality through a simple thought experiment. How does this affect your trust in divine revelation? When your limited mind grasps a proof of finitude, does it increase your awe of the Infinite Creator? Or do you still harbor doubts about His absolute power because you cannot fully comprehend it?

The Proof of Tatbiq: Impossibility of Infinite Dimensions
Taftazani expounds the proof of tatbiq with three formulations to demonstrate the impossibility of infinite dimensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logic of the tatbiq proof and why infinite dimensions lead to a contradiction in the priority-posteriority correlation.

Core Idea
Infinite dimensions fail because the correlation of priorities and posteriorities cannot be maintained.

This lesson unpacks one of the most subtle arguments in Islamic theology: the proof of tatbiq (application). Taftazani shows that if we try to apply the parts of an infinite dimension to each other, we run into a logical contradiction. The argument is abstract but powerful, relying on the paired concepts of priority and posteriority.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setup
The proof assumes an infinite dimension measured in cubits. Then we consider the application (comparison) between different parts of it.
2
First version: comparing thousands and units
If we compare the number of thousand-cubit units to the number of single cubits, we see that they cannot be in one-to-one correspondence, implying finitude.
This is similar to the proof of regression.
3
Second version: bounding between two limits
The distance from the start to any finite cubit is finite, so the whole cannot be infinite because each addition is only one cubit.
4
Third version: the core correlation argument
We consider the priority (closeness to start) and posteriority (distance from start) of each cubit. Matching them across the infinite series leads to an asymmetry that invalidates the correlation.
This is the main part of the passage.
5
Conclusion: infinite dimensions are impossible
The contradiction shows that the assumption of infinite dimensions leads to an absurdity in the fundamental relation of parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما على برهان التطبيق فمثل أن نفرض البعد الغير المتناهي أذرعاً، ثم نعتبر التطبيق بين عدة الألوف منها. وعدة الآحاد على ما مر في التسلسل أو يقال ما بين المبدأ المحقق أو المفروض، وبين كل ذراع متناه، . لكونه محصوراً بين حاصرين فيتناهى الكل، لأنه لا يزيد على ذلك إلا بواحد، أو يقال إلا ذراع مترتبة في الوضع، فنطبق بين قبلياتها وبعدياتها، فإن لم يتساويا [ بطل التضايف وإن تساويا ] لزم وجود ذراع له بعدية لا قبلية، لأن للمبدأ قبلية لا بعدية، وأيضاً إذا طبقنا وقعت قبلية الأول بإزاء بعدية الثاني، وقبلية الثاني بإزاء بعدية الثالث وهكذا إلى غير النهاية، فتبقى قبلية بلا بعدية فيبطل التضايف. وأيضاً للأول قبلية بلا بعدية فلو كان لكل ما عداه قبلية وبعدية معاً لزم قبلية بلا بعدية.
And as for the proof of application [tatbiq], such as that we assume the infinite dimension as cubits, then we consider the application between the number of its thousands and the number of its units, as has passed in the proof of regression. Or it is said: what is between the actual or assumed starting point and each cubit is finite, because it is bounded between two boundaries, so the whole is finite, because it does not increase beyond that except by one. Or it is said: except for cubits arranged in position, so we apply between their prior [qabliyyat] and posterior [ba'diyyat]. If they are not equal, the correlation [tada'uf] is invalidated. If they are equal, there necessarily exists a cubit that has posteriority without priority, because the starting point has priority without posteriority. Also, if we apply, the priority of the first aligns with the posteriority of the second, the priority of the second aligns with the posteriority of the third, and so on to infinity, so a priority remains without posteriority, thus the correlation is invalidated. Also, the first has priority without posteriority; if everything else had both priority and posteriority together, it would necessitate a priority without posteriority.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of tatbiq (application). It proceeds by assuming an infinite dimension measured in cubits. One then applies (compares) the number of thousands of cubits against the number of units (single cubits) from a starting point. Since the distance from the starting point to any given cubit is finite, the whole infinite series would have to be finite—each cubit adds only one, so if there are infinite cubits, the number of thousands would be infinite too, but the one-to-one correspondence fails. Alternatively, we consider the cubits arranged in order: each has a 'priority' (being closer to the start) and a 'posteriority' (being farther). If we match the priorities of one cubit with the posteriorities of the next, we get an infinite chain. If the two sets (priorities and posteriorities) are equal, then the starting cubit has priority without posteriority, breaking the correlation. If they are not equal, the correlation is invalid. Thus, infinite dimensions are impossible because they lead to asymmetry in the priority-posteriority relation, which is absurd for a dimension that is supposed to be uniform.

Key Terms
برهان التطبيق (burhan al-tatbiq)
القبلية (al-qabliyya)
البعدية (al-ba'diyya)
التضايف (al-tada'uf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of tatbiq is a physical measurement argument against infinite space.
Correction: It is a logical argument about the impossibility of maintaining the correlation (tada'uf) between priorities and posteriorities in an infinite series.

Checkpoint
What does the proof of tatbiq (application) show about infinite dimensions?
A) They can only be measured in thousand-cubit units.
B) The correlation of priorities and posteriorities leads to contradiction.
C) The starting point has both priority and posteriority.
D) All cubits have both priority and posteriority equally.

Key Takeaway
The proof of tatbiq demonstrates that infinite dimensions are logically impossible because they disrupt the necessary correlation between priority and posteriority in a series.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that every series must have a first element without a before. What in your life have you been treating as if it has no beginning, no source? How does recognizing that everything finite has a first change how you see your own existence? Will you now actively trace your blessings back to their true First Cause?
?
If infinite regression is impossible, then you and everything around you are contingent—dependent on something else. What does that mean for your sense of self-sufficiency? Are there areas where you falsely believe you are independent? How will you remind yourself daily of your neediness before the Eternal?
?
The proof forces a choice: either an infinite series (impossible) or a finite series with a beginning. Since you exist, you are part of a finite series. How does that truth confront your fear of endings or your desire for limitless worldly things? What specific attachment will you surrender today because it cannot be infinite?

First Objection: Differentiation in Space
Taftazani refutes the first objection that spatial differentiation implies real existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the opponent's argument from differentiation does not prove space is something real.

Core Idea
Differentiation does not entail reality — it may be mere illusion.

The first objection attempts to show that space cannot be pure nothing because different directions and sizes imply differentiation. Taftazani dismisses this as a mere illusion, teaching us that apparent differentiation does not necessitate actual existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutation
Read the Arabic passage for the first objection and its refutation. Notice the opponent's logical move from differentiation to reality.
The opponent uses a common-sense intuition.
2
Identify the key claim
Identify that the opponent claims that because different locations (south/north) have different properties, they must be real entities.
3
Understand the refutation
Taftazani says it's 'mere illusion' — the perception of difference does not prove objective reality.
This is a swift refutation relying on the principle that appearances can be deceptive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال احتج المخالف بوجوه: الأول: أن ما يلي الجنوب غير ما يلي الشمال وما يوازي ربع العالم أقل مما يوازي نصفه فلا يكون عدماً محضاً . قلنا مجرد وهم والثاني : أن الواقف على طرف العالم إما أن يمكنه مد اليد فثمة بعد، أو لا فثمة مانع . قلنا : لا يمكن لعدم الشرط لا لوجود المانع . الثالث: أن الجسم كلي لا ينحصر في شخص، فلا تتناهى أفراده الممكنة كسائر الكليات، بل توجد لعموم الفيض. قلنا الكلية لا تقتضي سوى إمكان كثرة أفراده المفروضة بالنظر إلى مفهومه، ولا ينافي امتناع كلها أو بعضها بموجب كلزوم المحالات المذكورة، على أن معنى إمكان افراده الغير المتناهية ليس اجتماعها في الوجود على ما هو المطلوب، بل عدم انتهائها إلى حد لا يمكن بعده وجود فرد آخر
He said: The opponent argued with [several] points: The first: That what is adjacent to the south is different from what is adjacent to the north, and what corresponds to a quarter of the world is less than what corresponds to half of it, so it is not pure non-existence. We said: [This is] mere illusion. The second: That the one standing at the edge of the world either can extend his hand, so there is an extension [beyond], or cannot, so there is an obstacle. We said: It cannot [be extended] due to the absence of the condition, not due to the presence of an obstacle. The third: That body is a universal [kulli] not restricted to a single individual, so its possible individuals are not finite, like other universals, but rather exist due to the generality of emanation [fayd]. We said: Universality implies only the possibility of a multiplicity of its individuals that are assumed with respect to its concept, and it does not contradict the impossibility of all or some of them due to the necessitation of the mentioned absurdities. Moreover, the meaning of the possibility of its infinite individuals is not their simultaneous existence in reality, as is demanded, but rather that they have no limit beyond which another individual cannot exist.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents three objections from someone who defends the possibility of infinite dimensions, along with their refutations. The first objection claims that since different directions (south/north) and different sizes (quarter/half) of the world imply differentiation, space cannot be pure nothingness. The refutation dismisses this as a mere illusion—differentiation does not prove actual extension. The second objection argues that if someone stands at the edge of the world, either they can extend their hand (meaning there is space beyond) or they cannot (then there is a barrier). The refutation states that the hand cannot extend not because of a barrier, but because the condition for extension (the existence of space) is absent. The third objection argues that 'body' is a universal concept, not restricted to a single individual; hence its possible instances are infinite, just like other universals, and they exist due to the generality of divine emanation. The refutation clarifies that universality implies only the abstract possibility of multiple instances, not their actual existence. The infinite individuals are only potential; their actual coexistence would lead to the absurdities already proven. In other words, possibility of infinite does not entail actual infinite existence.

Key Terms
المخالف (al-mukhalif)
العدم المحض (al-'adam al-mahd)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Taftazani refute the first objection about spatial differentiation?
A) He proves that south and north are the same.
B) He says it is mere illusion.
C) He argues that quarter and half are equal.
D) He accepts the objection but modifies it.

Key Takeaway
Perceived differentiation in space does not prove reality — it may be a mental illusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself comparing your life to others—using differences in location, wealth, or status—do you assume these differences prove that something real separates you? How would Taftazani's refutation challenge you to see those comparisons as mere illusion? Are you willing to release the imagined superiority or inferiority that comes from them?
?
The opponent used intellectual reasoning (quarter vs. half) to argue for the reality of space. Where in your own life do you rely on clever reasoning to justify attachments to things that are ultimately illusory—like the 'space' you occupy in someone's heart or a particular role you play? What would it cost you to call that reasoning 'mere illusion'?
?
If spatial differentiation is not real, then your sense of being 'far' from Allah or 'close' to Him is also an illusion. Right now, what imaginary distance have you created between yourself and your Creator? Will you let go of that illusion and recognize that nothing stands between you and Him except your own misconception?
