The Fourth Proof from Time
Al-Taftazani presents the fourth proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof for the eternity of the world, which argues that time must be eternal because any concept of non-existence before time requires time itself.

Core Idea
Time cannot be preceded by non-existence without already existing.

In this lesson, we examine the fourth argument presented by al-Taftazani for the eternity of the world. The argument is based on the nature of time. It claims that since non-existence cannot be conceived before time without invoking time, time must be eternal, and thus motion and the physical world are also eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note how the author states the premise and conclusion.
The proof is concise; each phrase carries weight.
2
Identify the key inference
The proof argues that precedence of non-existence over time is inconceivable without time, so time must exist at the moment of its non-existence (impossible). Therefore time is eternal.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Reflect on the implication
The proof concludes that if time is eternal, then motion (which is measured by time) and body (which is the subject of motion) must be eternal as well.
This connects to earlier proofs about motion and body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (الرابع) الرابع أن الزمان قديم، لأن سبق العدم عليه لا يتصور إلا بالزمان . فيلزم وجوده حين عدمه وقدمه يستلزم قدم الحركة والجسم لما مرّ . والجواب : أنه لم سلّم وجود الزمان بمعنى مقدار الحركة، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون تقدم العدم عليه ؟ كتقدم بعض أجزائه على البعض؟ والفرق بين التقدم والتأخر داخلان في مفهوم أجزاء الزمان دون عدم الحادث ووجوده ممنوع ولو سلّم فالمقصود منع انحصار أقسام السبق . لما كان الزمان أعني مقدار الحركة القائمة بالجسم قديماً، كان الجسم قديماً، أما اللزوم فظاهر، وأما حقيقة الملزوم ، ولأنه لو كان الزمان حادثاً أي مسبوقاً بالعدم،
He said: (The fourth) The fourth is that time is eternal, because precedence of non-existence over it is only conceivable by time. So its existence at the time of its non-existence follows, and its eternity necessitates the eternity of motion and body as previously mentioned. The answer: That it is not granted that time exists in the sense of the measure of motion. Why is it not permissible that non-existence precedes it like the precedence of some of its parts over others? And the distinction between priority and posteriority are included in the concept of the parts of time, not the non-existence of the originated event and its existence are prevented. Even if granted, the intended is the prevention of the confinement of the types of precedence. Since time, i.e., the measure of motion subsisting in body, is eternal, then the body is eternal. As for the implication, it is apparent; and as for the reality of the implied, and because if time were originated, i.e., preceded by non-existence, ...
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof for the eternity of the world based on time, and the author's refutation. The proof states that time must be eternal because the concept of non-existence before time requires time itself (circular). Therefore time is eternal, leading to the eternity of motion and body. The author responds by denying the premise that time exists in the sense of the measure of motion, and argues that non-existence could precede time analogously to how one part of time precedes another. The distinction between priority and posteriority is internal to time, not applicable to the non-existence or existence of a originated event. Then the author discusses the implication further, stating that if time is eternal, then body is eternal, but the reality of the implied is questioned, and mentions that if time were originated, then... The response is cut off, indicating the argument continues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that time is a self-subsistent entity that can be imagined without motion.
Correction: The proof assumes time is the measure of motion, as established earlier. It does not treat time as an independent entity.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth proof, why must time be eternal?
A) Because time is infinite
B) Because non-existence before time implies time exists beforehand
C) Because motion is eternal
D) Because the world is eternal

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof attempts to establish the eternity of time by arguing that priority of non-existence over time is inconceivable without time.

Refutation of the Fourth Proof from Time
Al-Taftazani refutes the fourth proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's response to the fourth proof, challenging the premise that time exists as an eternal measure of motion and proposing an alternative analysis of precedence.

Core Idea
The proof fails because time's existence is not granted as an objective measure; non-existence can precede time as one part precedes another.

Al-Taftazani now responds to the fourth proof. He questions the assumption that time exists as an eternal measure of motion. He suggests that non-existence could precede time in the same way that one part of time precedes another. The argument also critiques the confinement of types of precedence and discusses the implication if time were eternal versus originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the Arabic passage for the refutation. Note that the author starts with 'والجواب' (The answer).
The response is multi-layered.
2
Identify the first objection
The first move is to deny that time exists in the sense of a measure of motion. The author asks: why can't non-existence precede time like parts of time precede each other?
This draws an analogy with temporal parts.
3
Understand the distinction about precedence
The author argues that priority and posteriority are internal to time, not applicable to the non-existence of originated events. He then says even if granted, the goal is to prevent confining types of precedence.
This is a subtle logical point.
4
Consider the conditional implication
The author then discusses: if time (as measure of motion) is eternal, then body is eternal. But he questions the reality of the implied, and mentions the possibility of time being originated.
The passage cuts off, but the direction is clear.

6 min
The Fourth Proof for the Pre-Eternity of the World and Its Refutation
Presentation and refutation of the fourth proof for the world's pre-eternity based on time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof for the world's pre-eternity based on time and the multi-layered refutation that denies the restriction of precedence to five types.

Core Idea
The refutation breaks the proof by showing precedence of non-existence over time need not be temporal.

Sanusi presents a cosmological proof that argues time must be pre-eternal, then refutes it by examining the nature of precedence. The argument is dense and requires careful tracking of logical moves. This lesson walks through the proof and its refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall flow. Notice the structure: proof, initial objection, classification of precedence, further objections and answers.
The passage uses technical terms like 'precedence by nature' and 'by time'.
2
Identify the core proof
The proof claims time is pre-eternal because its non-existence would require a prior time, leading to a contradiction. From this, it infers time is pre-eternal, and since time is the measure of motion, motion and body are also pre-eternal.
This proof relies on the impossibility of time being preceded by non-existence without time.
3
Follow the first refutation stage
The refutation begins by questioning why the precedence of non-existence over time cannot be like the precedence of one part of time over another, which is intrinsic and not temporal in the standard sense.
This challenges the assumption that any precedence must be one of the five known types.
4
Examine the classification of precedence
The refutation systematically rejects causality, honor, rank, and nature as applicable to time's non-existence, then argues that temporal precedence would be absurd. It then denies the exhaustiveness of the five types, citing precedence among time's parts as a counterexample.
The key move is showing that precedence among time's parts is not temporal in the sense required by the proof.
5
Synthesize the takeaway
Understand that the proof fails because it assumes a single notion of temporal precedence, while the refutation shows non-temporal precedence is possible. This weakens the argument for the world's pre-eternity from time.
This refutation is part of a larger series of arguments in kalam cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (الرابع) دليل رابع على قدم العالم والرد عليه الرابع أن الزمان(۱) قديم، لأن سبق العدم عليه لا يتصور إلا بالزمان . فيلزم وجوده حين عدمه وقدمه يستلزم قدم الحركة والجسم لما مرّ . والجواب : أنه لم سلّم وجود الزمان بمعنى مقدار الحركة، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون تقدم العدم عليه ؟ كتقدم بعض أجزائه على البعض؟ والفرق بين التقدم والتأخر داخلان في مفهوم أجزاء الزمان دون عدم الحادث ووجوده ممنوع
فسبق العدم عليه لا يكون بالعلية أو الشرف أو الرتبة ، وهو ظاهر، ولا بالطبع، لأن الزمان ،ممكن والممكن يقتضي لا استحقاقية الوجود والعدم نظرا الى ذاته، فلا يفتقر بذاته إلى عدمه كيف والمتقدم بالطبع يجامع المتأخر، وعدم الشيء لا يجامع وجوده فتعين أن يكون بالزمان وهو أيضاً محال لاستلزامه وجود الزمان حين عدمه، لأن معنى المتقدم بالزمان أن يوجد المتقدم في زمان لا يوجد فيه المتأخر .
والجواب : بعد تسليم وجود الزمان عبارة عن مقدار الحركة. أنا لا نسلم انحصار أقسام السبق في الخمسة المذكورة 1 بالمعاني المذكورة ] (۱) لأن سبق أجزاء الزمان بعضها على البعض خارج عن ذلك فليكن سبق عدم الزمان على وجوده كذلك. لا يقال التقدم والتأخر داخلان في مفهوم أجزاء الزمان فإن تقدم الأمس على الغد ظاهر بالنظر الى نفس مفهومه، ولا كذلك حال عدم الحادث بالنسبة الى وجوده لأنا نقول : إنما جاز ذلك من جهة أن الأمس اسم للزمان المأخوذة مع التقدم المخصوص، وإما في نفس أجزاء الزمان فلا بل غايته لزوم التقدم والتأخر فيما بينها ، لكونها عبارة عن اتصال غير قار. ولو سلم، فالحادث من حيث الحدوث أيضاً كذلك، إذ لا معنى له سوى ما يكون وجوده مسبوقاً بالعدم .
ولو سلم. فالمقصود منع انحصار السبق في الأقسام الخمسة مستنداً الى السبق فيما بين أجزاء الزمان، فإنه ليس زمانياً بمعنى أن يوجد المتقدم في زمان لا يوجد فيه المتأخر، ولا يضرنا تسميته زمانياً بمعنى آخر، وقد سبق تحقيق ذلك في موضعه .
He said (the fourth): A fourth proof for the pre-eternity of the world and its refutation. The fourth [proof] is that time is pre-eternal, because its being preceded by non-existence cannot be conceived except by [means of] time. So its existence at the time of its non-existence follows, and its pre-eternity entails the pre-eternity of motion and body as has passed. The answer: [We say] even if it is granted that time exists in the sense of the measure of motion, why may it not be that its being preceded by non-existence is like the precedence of some of its parts over others? The difference between precedence and posteriority are included in the concept of the parts of time, but not [in the concept of] the non-existence and existence of the temporal event. This is prevented. Then the precedence of non-existence over it cannot be by causality, honor, or rank—that is clear—nor by nature, because time is contingent, and the contingent by its essence does not warrant existence or non-existence; thus it does not by itself require its non-existence. How [could it be] when that which is preceded by nature coexists with the later, while the non-existence of something does not coexist with its existence. So it is determined that it must be by time, but that is also impossible because it entails the existence of time at the time of its non-existence, since the meaning of 'preceded by time' is that the earlier exists in a time in which the later does not exist. The answer: After granting that time is an expression for the measure of motion, we do not concede that the divisions of precedence are restricted to the five mentioned in the mentioned senses, because the precedence of some parts of time over others is outside that [classification]. So let the precedence of the non-existence of time over its existence be likewise. It cannot be said: 'Precedence and posteriority are included in the concept of the parts of time, for the precedence of yesterday over tomorrow is apparent with respect to its very concept, unlike the case of the non-existence of a temporal event relative to its existence.' For we say: That is only permissible from the aspect that 'yesterday' is a name for time taken with specific precedence, but with respect to the parts of time themselves, no; rather, the utmost is the necessary [connection] of precedence and posteriority among them, since they are expressions for a non-stationary continuum. And if it is granted, the temporal event from the aspect of temporality is also thus, since nothing is meant by it except that its existence is preceded by non-existence. And if it is granted, then the goal is to deny the restriction of precedence to the five divisions, based on the precedence among the parts of time, for it is not temporal in the sense that the earlier exists in a time in which the later does not exist, and it does not harm us to call it temporal in another sense. And verification of this has passed in its place.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the fourth proof for the pre-eternity of the world. The proof argues that time is pre-eternal because its being preceded by non-existence would itself require time, leading to an absurdity. Therefore time is pre-eternal, and since time is the measure of motion, motion and body are also pre-eternal. The refutation first questions the necessity of temporal precedence: perhaps the precedence of non-existence over time is like the precedence of one part of time over another, which is intrinsic to time's parts. It then examines the standard classification of types of precedence (by cause, honor, rank, nature, time) and argues that none apply to the non-existence of time. The only remaining possibility, temporal precedence, is absurd as it would require time to exist before itself. The answer then denies that the five divisions are exhaustive, citing the precedence among parts of time as a counterexample. A potential objection is addressed: although 'yesterday' and 'tomorrow' have conceptual precedence, this is due to their names, not the parts of time themselves. The passage concludes that the non-existence of time can be conceived as a non-temporal precedence, thus breaking the proof.

القدم
السبق
الحركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the refutation simply asserts that time is not pre-eternal without argument, or that it denies any kind of precedence for non-existence.
Correction: The refutation does not deny precedence; it denies that the precedence must be temporal. It offers a detailed analysis of types of precedence and shows that non-existence of time can be prior in a non-temporal way, similar to the intrinsic order of time's parts.

Checkpoint
Why does the refutation argue that precedence by nature cannot apply to the non-existence of time?
A) Because time is not a natural entity.
B) Because the contingent does not necessitate its own non-existence, and natural precedence requires coexistence.
C) Because time is pre-eternal by nature.
D) Because nature only applies to bodies.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof collapses because the precedence of non-existence over time need not be temporal; the refutation shows that the five types of precedence are not exhaustive, and a non-temporal precedence is coherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have seen that the refutation denies that the precedence of non-existence over time must be temporal. In your own life, you often assume that the causes and origins of your struggles must fit into your familiar categories. Where have you, like the proponents of the proof, boxed God's absolute power into your own limited understanding? Will you actively challenge that assumption starting today?
?
The text shows that the precedence of yesterday over tomorrow is not a temporal precedence in the ordinary sense, but a non-temporal one inherent to time's continuum. Do you ever think of your past sins as merely 'before' in chronological time, without recognizing that they have a non-temporal precedence in God's eternal knowledge? How will you let this insight reshape your sense of accountability and repentance?
?
The proof tried to limit precedence to five categories, but the refutation broke that framework. Are there categories in your faith—like your image of God's mercy or judgment—that you have unconsciously narrowed? What is one category you will re-examine tonight, armed with the lesson that reality is not exhausted by your mental divisions?

Objection and Answer on the Types of Precedence
Objection and answer on the types of precedence, focusing on time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that precedence by time is the only option, by denying that the five types of precedence are exhaustive.

Core Idea
The five types of precedence are not exhaustive; even parts of time escape them.

This passage presents a sharp objection-answer exchange. The objector attempts to force a conclusion that the precedence of the world's non-existence must be by time, then shows the absurdity that follows. The author skillfully responds by questioning the completeness of the list of precedence types, using the precedence among parts of time as a counterexample. This lesson unpacks the logical moves and clarifies the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to get an overall sense of the argument. Note the back-and-forth structure: an objection followed by a detailed answer.
The passage is dense; read twice if needed.
2
Identify the objection
Find the statement where the objector claims precedence must be by time, and what problem arises from that. Underline the reasoning: cause, honor, rank, and nature are ruled out, so time remains, but time leads to contradiction.
The objector is assuming only five types exist.
3
Follow the answer's key move
Notice how the author first concedes the definition of time, then denies that the five types are exhaustive. The example of parts of time (e.g., yesterday and tomorrow) shows a form of precedence not captured by the five.
This is the central refutation: the enumeration is incomplete.
4
Reflect on the refinements
The author further discusses the nature of time as a 'non-stationary continuum' and argues that even if the objection's points are granted, the event itself is defined as preceded by non-existence. The ultimate goal is to deny the limitation to five types.
This shows the depth of the author's dialectical method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فسبق العدم عليه لا يكون بالعلية أو الشرف أو الرتبة، وهو ظاهر، ولا بالطبع، لأن الزمان ممكن والممكن يقتضي لا استحقاقية الوجود والعدم نظرا الى ذاته، فلا يفتقر بذاته إلى عدمه كيف والمتقدم بالطبع يجامع المتأخر، وعدم الشيء لا يجامع وجوده فتعين أن يكون بالزمان وهو أيضاً محال لاستلزامه وجود الزمان حين عدمه، لأن معنى المتقدم بالزمان أن يوجد المتقدم في زمان لا يوجد فيه المتأخر. والجواب: بعد تسليم وجود الزمان عبارة عن مقدار الحركة. أنا لا نسلم انحصار أقسام السبق في الخمسة المذكورة بالمعاني المذكورة، لأن سبق أجزاء الزمان بعضها على البعض خارج عن ذلك فليكن سبق عدم الزمان على وجوده كذلك. لا يقال التقدم والتأخر داخلان في مفهوم أجزاء الزمان فإن تقدم الأمس على الغد ظاهر بالنظر الى نفس مفهومه، ولا كذلك حال عدم الحادث بالنسبة الى وجوده لأنا نقول: إنما جاز ذلك من جهة أن الأمس اسم للزمان المأخوذة مع التقدم المخصوص، وأما في نفس أجزاء الزمان فلا بل غايته لزوم التقدم والتأخر فيما بينها، لكونها عبارة عن اتصال غير قار. ولو سلم، فالحادث من حيث الحدوث أيضاً كذلك، إذ لا معنى له سوى ما يكون وجوده مسبوقاً بالعدم. ولو سلم. فالمقصود منع انحصار السبق في الأقسام الخمسة مستنداً الى السبق فيما بين أجزاء الزمان، فإنه ليس زمانياً بمعنى أن يوجد المتقدم في زمان لا يوجد فيه المتأخر، ولا يضرنا تسميته زمانياً بمعنى آخر، وقد سبق تحقيق ذلك في موضعه.
Thus the precedence of non-existence over it (the world) cannot be by causality, honor, or rank, and that is apparent; nor by nature, because time is possible and the possible necessitates no entitlement to existence or non-existence in itself, so it is not in need of its non-existence in itself—how so? The naturally prior coexists with the posterior, whereas the non-existence of a thing does not coexist with its existence. So it is determined that it is by time, but that too is impossible because it entails the existence of time at the time of its non-existence, for the meaning of 'prior by time' is that the prior exists in a time in which the posterior does not exist. The answer: after conceding that time is a measure of motion, we do not accept that the divisions of precedence are limited to the five mentioned with the mentioned meanings, because the precedence of some parts of time over others is outside that, so let the precedence of the non-existence of time over its existence be likewise. It cannot be said that priority and posteriority are included in the concept of the parts of time, for the priority of yesterday over tomorrow is apparent with regard to its very concept, and not so the state of the non-existence of an event relative to its existence. For we say: that is permissible only because 'yesterday' is a name for time taken with a specific priority, but regarding the parts of time themselves, no; rather the utmost is the necessity of priority and posteriority among them, because they are a non-stationary continuum. And even if conceded, the event as event is also like that, since its meaning is nothing other than that its existence is preceded by non-existence. And even if conceded, the point is to deny the limitation of precedence to the five divisions, based on the precedence among parts of time, for it is not temporal in the sense that the prior exists in a time in which the posterior does not exist, nor does it harm us to call it temporal in another sense, and the verification of that has already preceded in its place.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer concerning the types of precedence (sabq) that could apply to the non-existence of the world relative to its existence. The objector argues that precedence of non-existence over existence cannot be by cause, honor, rank, or nature, so it must be by time. But that is impossible because it would require time to exist when the world does not. The answer refuses to accept that the five types of precedence are exhaustive. The author points out that the precedence of some parts of time over others is not 'time-based' in the same sense, so the precedence of the non-existence of time over its existence can be similar. This demonstrates that the objection's enumeration is not airtight. The discussion proceeds with logical refinements about the concept of parts of time and the nature of events, ultimately asserting that the goal is to deny the limitation, not to concede the philosophers' notion of time.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That precedence by time is the only remaining option once other types are ruled out, and that this forces an absurd conclusion.
Correction: The author shows that the enumeration of five types is not exhaustive, so the objection's reasoning is based on an incomplete premise. The precedence of parts of time provides a counterexample.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the answer to the objection about precedence by time?
A) It accepts that precedence must be by time.
B) It denies that the five types of precedence are exhaustive, citing the precedence of parts of time.
C) It argues that time does not exist.
D) It claims that precedence is not needed at all.

Key Takeaway
The five types of precedence are not exhaustive; the precedence of the world's non-existence over its existence does not require a temporal interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would change if you woke each morning with the awareness that Allah created you from nothing and could return you to nothing at any moment?
?
The objector assumed that time must exist before the world. Do you ever assume that your daily routines and schedules are absolute, forgetting that time itself is a created measure? Will you live today submitting to the Owner of time rather than being a slave to the clock?
?
The author denies that the list of precedence types is complete. In your own thinking, have you limited God’s power by assuming that creation must follow familiar patterns of causality or time? What presumption about how God must act do you need to surrender right now?

The Philosophers' Proof of the Encompassing Sphere and Its Refutation
Al-Taftazani refutes the philosophers' proof for the muhaddid based on the impossibility of void, bodily difference, and natural motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three premises of the philosophers' argument for the muhaddid and how the Ash'ari positions on void, bodily similarity, and divine power refute it.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari refutation rests on affirming the possibility of void, similarity of bodies, and that all motion is by God's will.

Al-Taftazani begins by laying out the philosophers' argument for the necessity of an outermost sphere (muhaddid). He then presents the Ash'ari counter-positions that undermine the entire proof. This lesson focuses on the clash between natural causation and divine power in the debate over celestial motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the flow.
Focus on the logical structure: premises, counter-premises, conclusion.
2
Identify the three premises
The philosophers' proof depends on impossibility of void, real difference of bodies, and natural motion. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the Ash'ari replies
Note how al-Taftazani asserts void is possible, bodies are similar, and all motion is by divine power, not nature.
This is the crux of the refutation.
4
See the implications
If the proof fails, the derived properties (no rupture, generation, etc.) also fail. The Ash'aris accept these properties only from revelation, not philosophy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (تنبيه)
إثبات المحدد مبنى على امتناع الخلاء
لما كان عندنا الخلاء ممكناً، والأجسام متماثلة، والحركات مستندة إلى قدرة المختار، لم يتم ما ذكروه، ولم تمنع الحركة المستقيمة على السموات ولم تثبت ما فرعوا على ذلك، من أنها لا تقبل الخرق والالتئام، ولا الكون والفساد، ولا الكيفيات الفعلية والانفعالية ونحو ذلك، وزعم بعض القدماء أنها في غاية الصلابة واليبس والملاسة ولها في تمارسها نغمات يسمعها أصحاب الرياضة.
لا خفاء في أن إثبات المحدد مبنى على امتناع الخلاء، وإلا لجاز أن تنتهي إليه الامتدادات وتتعين به أوضاع الجهات، وعلى اختلاف الأجسام بالحقيقة، واستناد بعض حركاتها إلى الطبيع، وإلا لما كان من الأجسام ما يقتضي صوب المحيط ويتحرك إليه بالطبع، ومنها ما يقتضي صوب المركز ويتحرك إليه بالطبع، فلم يكن العلو والسفل جهتين طبيعيتين، ولما كان عندنا أن الخلاء ممكن، وأن الأجسام متماثلة، يجوز على كل منهما ما يجوز على الآخر، وأن الحركات مستندة إلى قدرة الفاعل المختار لا أثر فيها للطبيعة، لم يتم ما ذكروه في إثبات المحدد بالتفسير المذكور، ولم تمتنع الحركة المستقيمة على السموات كما لم تمتنع على العناصر التحقق الجهات بدونها، ولم يثبت ما فرعوا على إثبات المحدد، وعدم قبوله الحركة المستقيمة من أن السموات لا تقبل الخرق والالتئام، ولا الكون والفساد ولا الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة، ولا الألوان والطعوم، والروائح ولا اللين والصلابة والخشونة والملاسة ولا الخفة والثقل إلى غير ذلك مما ورد به الشريعة المطهرة، على أنه لو تم ما ذكر ففي المحدد خاصة دون سائر الأفلاك. فإن تمسكوا بأنه علم بالرصد أنها تتحرك على الاستدارة فيكون فيها مبدأ ميل مستدير فلا تتحرك على الاستقامة، لامتناع اجتماع المثلين.
قلنا لو سلّم ذلك، فامتناع انقطاع الاستدارة، وحدوث الاستقامة لم يعلم بالرصد ودليل سرمدية الحركات لم يتم. كيف وقد جعلوها إرادية لا ذاتية، يمتنع انفكاكها وزعم جماعة من قدماء الحكماء المتألهين أن الأفلاك في غاية
He said (Note): The proof of the muhaddid (encompassing sphere) is based on the impossibility of void. Since with us void is possible, bodies are similar, and motions are dependent on the power of the Chosen One (al-Mukhtar), what they mentioned is not established, and straight motion is not prevented in the heavens, and what they derived from that—that they do not accept rupture and rejoining, nor generation and corruption, nor active and passive qualities, etc.—is not established. And some ancients claimed that they are in utmost hardness, dryness, and smoothness, and that in their motion they have melodies heard by the practitioners of spiritual exercises. There is no concealment that the proof of the muhaddid is based on the impossibility of void, otherwise extensions could end at it and directions' positions could be determined by it, and on the real difference of bodies, and on some of their motions being based on nature; otherwise there would not be among bodies those that require the direction of the circumference and move towards it naturally, and those that require the direction of the center and move towards it naturally, so high and low would not be natural directions. And since with us void is possible, bodies are similar—what is possible for one is possible for the other—and motions are dependent on the power of the Free Agent (al-Fa'il al-Mukhtar) with no effect of nature in them, what they mentioned in proving the muhaddid according to the aforementioned interpretation is not established, straight motion is not prevented in the heavens just as it is not prevented in the elements without it, and what they derived from the proof of the muhaddid and its not accepting straight motion—that the heavens do not accept rupture and rejoining, nor generation and corruption, nor heat and cold, moisture and dryness, nor colors, tastes, odors, nor softness, hardness, roughness, smoothness, nor lightness and heaviness, etc., beyond what the pure Shari'ah has conveyed—is not established. Moreover, even if what was mentioned were established, it would be specific to the muhaddid, not to the other spheres. If they argue that it is known by observation that they move in a circle, so they have a principle of circular inclination and do not move in a straight line, due to the impossibility of two likes combining, we say: Even if that is granted, the impossibility of the cessation of circular motion and the occurrence of straight motion is not known by observation, and the proof of the perpetuity of motions is not established. How so, when they have made them voluntary, not essential, impossible to separate? And a group of ancient divine philosophers claimed that the spheres are in utmost...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by al-Taftazani of the philosophers' argument for the existence of the muhaddid (the outermost sphere) and the properties they attribute to the celestial spheres. The passage begins by stating the philosophers' basis: their proof of the muhaddid depends on three premises: (1) the impossibility of void, (2) the real difference between celestial and elemental bodies (so that some naturally move toward the circumference and others toward the center), and (3) that some motions are natural. Al-Taftazani then delivers the Ash'ari response: since we hold that void is possible, that all bodies are similar in essence (so what is possible for one is possible for another), and that all motions are directly caused by the divine will (al-qudra al-mukhtar) with no natural necessity, the philosophers' argument fails. Consequently, straight motion is not impossible for the heavens, and the derived properties (like not admitting rupture, generation, corruption, etc.) are not established. He adds that even if the proof of the muhaddid were sound, it would apply only to the outermost sphere, not to all spheres. An objection is then raised: observation shows the heavens move circularly, implying a natural circular inclination that prevents straight motion, because two opposing inclinations cannot coexist in one body. Al-Taftazani answers that the impossibility of ceasing circular motion and beginning straight motion is not known by observation; moreover, the philosophers themselves claim the motion of the spheres is voluntary (irada) rather than essential (dhatiyya), so it is not impossible for them to change. The passage ends with a remark about ancient divine philosophers who held that the spheres are in extreme hardness, etc.

Key Terms
المحدد (al-muhaddid)
الخلاء (al-khala')
الحركة المستقيمة (al-haraka al-mustaqima)
القدرة المختار (al-qudra al-mukhtar)
الطبيعة (al-tabi'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ash'ari acceptance of void means they believe in a physical vacuum within the cosmos.
Correction: The void discussed here is empty space beyond the outermost sphere, not a vacuum within the universe. The Ash'aris do not necessarily affirm a vacuum elsewhere.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani, why does the philosophers' proof of the muhaddid fail?
A) Because observation proves the heavens move in straight lines.
B) Because the Ash'aris affirm the impossibility of void.
C) Because the Ash'aris hold that void is possible, bodies are similar, and motions are by divine power.
D) Because the philosophers themselves admitted the spheres are composed of the same matter as elements.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari positions on void, bodily similarity, and divine power nullify the philosophical argument for an outermost sphere, showing that celestial motion is not governed by natural necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all motion in the universe, including the beating of your heart and the thoughts in your mind, is directly caused by God's power every moment, do you truly live as if He is perpetually present and active in your life? Or do you unconsciously attribute things to 'nature', 'habit', or 'chance'? Will you pause right now and consciously acknowledge His immediate hand in your next breath?
?
The philosophers argued that celestial bodies are perfect and incorruptible based on reason, while the Ash'aris insisted on relying on revelation. In your own life, where do you trust your limited reasoning over God's revealed guidance? Are there areas where you assume you 'know better' than scripture? Will you commit to prioritizing revelation over your own judgment in at least one specific matter today?
?
Al-Taftazani states that even if the philosophers' proof were sound, it would only apply to the outermost sphere, not the others. This shows how even a small error in reasoning can lead to sweeping conclusions. Where in your beliefs have you built a large edifice on a shaky foundation? Are you willing to examine and correct it, even if it means uprooting comfortable assumptions?

The Philosophers' Objection from Circular Motion and al-Taftazani's Response
Al-Taftazani responds to the philosophers' objection based on observed circular motion of the heavens.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' objection that observed circular motion prevents straight motion due to impossibility of two inclinations, and al-Taftazani's counter that the motion is voluntary, not natural, and thus changeable.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari response shows that the assumed essential inclination for circular motion is not proven, and voluntary motion can cease.

After refuting the main proof, al-Taftazani addresses the philosophers' strongest objection: observation shows the heavens move circularly, so they must have a natural circular inclination that prevents straight motion. This lesson unpacks his clever reply, pointing out that the motion is deemed voluntary by the philosophers themselves, undermining their own objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The philosophers argue that observation shows circular motion, implying a natural inclination that prevents straight motion due to impossibility of two opposites in one body.
2
Understand al-Taftazani's response
He says even if we grant that, the impossibility of cessation of circular motion is not known by observation; the proof of perpetual motion is not established.
3
Note the key point
The philosophers themselves say the motion is voluntary (irada), not essential; voluntary motion can change, so it is not impossible for straight motion to occur.
4
Consider the final remark
Al-Taftazani mentions ancient philosophers who held the spheres to be extremely hard, etc., but this is cut off in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (تنبيه)
إثبات المحدد مبنى على امتناع الخلاء
لما كان عندنا الخلاء ممكناً، والأجسام متماثلة، والحركات مستندة إلى قدرة المختار، لم يتم ما ذكروه، ولم تمنع الحركة المستقيمة على السموات ولم تثبت ما فرعوا على ذلك، من أنها لا تقبل الخرق والالتئام، ولا الكون والفساد، ولا الكيفيات الفعلية والانفعالية ونحو ذلك، وزعم بعض القدماء أنها في غاية الصلابة واليبس والملاسة ولها في تمارسها نغمات يسمعها أصحاب الرياضة.
لا خفاء في أن إثبات المحدد مبنى على امتناع الخلاء، وإلا لجاز أن تنتهي إليه الامتدادات وتتعين به أوضاع الجهات، وعلى اختلاف الأجسام بالحقيقة، واستناد بعض حركاتها إلى الطبيع، وإلا لما كان من الأجسام ما يقتضي صوب المحيط ويتحرك إليه بالطبع، ومنها ما يقتضي صوب المركز ويتحرك إليه بالطبع، فلم يكن العلو والسفل جهتين طبيعيتين، ولما كان عندنا أن الخلاء ممكن، وأن الأجسام متماثلة، يجوز على كل منهما ما يجوز على الآخر، وأن الحركات مستندة إلى قدرة الفاعل المختار لا أثر فيها للطبيعة، لم يتم ما ذكروه في إثبات المحدد بالتفسير المذكور، ولم تمتنع الحركة المستقيمة على السموات كما لم تمتنع على العناصر التحقق الجهات بدونها، ولم يثبت ما فرعوا على إثبات المحدد، وعدم قبوله الحركة المستقيمة من أن السموات لا تقبل الخرق والالتئام، ولا الكون والفساد ولا الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة، ولا الألوان والطعوم، والروائح ولا اللين والصلابة والخشونة والملاسة ولا الخفة والثقل إلى غير ذلك مما ورد به الشريعة المطهرة، على أنه لو تم ما ذكر ففي المحدد خاصة دون سائر الأفلاك. فإن تمسكوا بأنه علم بالرصد أنها تتحرك على الاستدارة فيكون فيها مبدأ ميل مستدير فلا تتحرك على الاستقامة، لامتناع اجتماع المثلين.
قلنا لو سلّم ذلك، فامتناع انقطاع الاستدارة، وحدوث الاستقامة لم يعلم بالرصد ودليل سرمدية الحركات لم يتم. كيف وقد جعلوها إرادية لا ذاتية، يمتنع انفكاكها وزعم جماعة من قدماء الحكماء المتألهين أن الأفلاك في غاية
He said (Note): The proof of the muhaddid (encompassing sphere) is based on the impossibility of void. Since with us void is possible, bodies are similar, and motions are dependent on the power of the Chosen One (al-Mukhtar), what they mentioned is not established, and straight motion is not prevented in the heavens, and what they derived from that—that they do not accept rupture and rejoining, nor generation and corruption, nor active and passive qualities, etc.—is not established. And some ancients claimed that they are in utmost hardness, dryness, and smoothness, and that in their motion they have melodies heard by the practitioners of spiritual exercises. There is no concealment that the proof of the muhaddid is based on the impossibility of void, otherwise extensions could end at it and directions' positions could be determined by it, and on the real difference of bodies, and on some of their motions being based on nature; otherwise there would not be among bodies those that require the direction of the circumference and move towards it naturally, and those that require the direction of the center and move towards it naturally, so high and low would not be natural directions. And since with us void is possible, bodies are similar—what is possible for one is possible for the other—and motions are dependent on the power of the Free Agent (al-Fa'il al-Mukhtar) with no effect of nature in them, what they mentioned in proving the muhaddid according to the aforementioned interpretation is not established, straight motion is not prevented in the heavens just as it is not prevented in the elements without it, and what they derived from the proof of the muhaddid and its not accepting straight motion—that the heavens do not accept rupture and rejoining, nor generation and corruption, nor heat and cold, moisture and dryness, nor colors, tastes, odors, nor softness, hardness, roughness, smoothness, nor lightness and heaviness, etc., beyond what the pure Shari'ah has conveyed—is not established. Moreover, even if what was mentioned were established, it would be specific to the muhaddid, not to the other spheres. If they argue that it is known by observation that they move in a circle, so they have a principle of circular inclination and do not move in a straight line, due to the impossibility of two likes combining, we say: Even if that is granted, the impossibility of the cessation of circular motion and the occurrence of straight motion is not known by observation, and the proof of the perpetuity of motions is not established. How so, when they have made them voluntary, not essential, impossible to separate? And a group of ancient divine philosophers claimed that the spheres are in utmost...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by al-Taftazani of the philosophers' argument for the existence of the muhaddid (the outermost sphere) and the properties they attribute to the celestial spheres. The passage begins by stating the philosophers' basis: their proof of the muhaddid depends on three premises: (1) the impossibility of void, (2) the real difference between celestial and elemental bodies (so that some naturally move toward the circumference and others toward the center), and (3) that some motions are natural. Al-Taftazani then delivers the Ash'ari response: since we hold that void is possible, that all bodies are similar in essence (so what is possible for one is possible for another), and that all motions are directly caused by the divine will (al-qudra al-mukhtar) with no natural necessity, the philosophers' argument fails. Consequently, straight motion is not impossible for the heavens, and the derived properties (like not admitting rupture, generation, corruption, etc.) are not established. He adds that even if the proof of the muhaddid were sound, it would apply only to the outermost sphere, not to all spheres. An objection is then raised: observation shows the heavens move circularly, implying a natural circular inclination that prevents straight motion, because two opposing inclinations cannot coexist in one body. Al-Taftazani answers that the impossibility of ceasing circular motion and beginning straight motion is not known by observation; moreover, the philosophers themselves claim the motion of the spheres is voluntary (irada) rather than essential (dhatiyya), so it is not impossible for them to change. The passage ends with a remark about ancient divine philosophers who held that the spheres are in extreme hardness, etc.

Key Terms
الحركة الاستدارية (al-haraka al-istidariyya)
الميل المستدير (al-mayl al-mustadir)
الحركة الإرادية (al-haraka al-iradiyya)
الحركة الذاتية (al-haraka al-dhatiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani, what undermines the philosophers' objection that circular motion prevents straight motion?
A) The observation of circular motion is false.
B) The impossibility of change is not known by observation and the motion is voluntary.
C) The spheres are made of different matter than elements.
D) Straight motion is actually observed in the heavens.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani refutes the objection from circular motion by asserting that the impossibility of change is not empirically proven and that the motion is voluntary, not essential, so straight motion remains possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the philosophers assumed circular motion must be essential, but al-Taftazani countered that it is voluntary. In your own life, are there habits or patterns you assume are 'unchangeable' about yourself, but which are actually voluntary choices you have the power to alter? What would it take for you to move in a new 'straight line' starting today?
?
The argument from observation seemed convincing, yet al-Taftazani pointed out that observation does not show impossibility. When have you accepted something as 'impossible' based only on what you have seen, without considering that change could come? Are you willing to reexamine a belief you hold that may be based on limited observation?
?
Al-Taftazani's response hinges on the distinction between voluntary and essential. This lesson challenges you to own that many of your actions are voluntary, not forced by nature. Is there an area of your spiritual life where you have felt 'stuck' in a pattern, blaming circumstances or habit, but now realize you can voluntarily choose a new direction? Will you commit to one concrete change this week?

Motions of the Representative Spheres: Two Opinions
Sanusī presents two opinions on representative sphere motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions on the cause of motion of the representative spheres (excluding the moon's) and the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The spheres' motion is either borrowed from the eighth sphere or self-generated.

In this passage, al-Sanūsī presents a debate among scholars regarding the motions of the 'representative spheres' beyond the moon's sphere. These spheres exhibit motions at apogees and perigees that align with the rotation of the eighth sphere (the sphere of fixed stars). Two positions arise: one attributes this motion entirely to the eighth sphere, while the other insists the spheres move by their own essence to avoid being purposeless. Let's examine the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the overall argument. Note the two groups of scholars mentioned.
The passage uses technical terms like 'الأفلاك الممثلة' and 'الفلك الثامن'.
2
Identify the two opinions
Identify the two opinions: (1) the representative spheres move by the motion of the eighth sphere; (2) they move by themselves. Notice the reason given for the second opinion: to avoid them being idle (عطلاً).
The second group also argues that the container (eighth sphere) does not necessarily move the contained.
3
Reflect on the underlying principle
Consider why the second group rejects the necessity of the eighth sphere's motion. The principle 'the mover of the container does not necessarily move the contained' is a key logical point.
This reflects a broader debate in Islamic cosmology about causation and autonomy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حركاتها إلى التوالي، فمنها حركات الأفلاك الممثلة سوى ممثل القمر، وتظهر في الأوجات والحضيضات وهي على وفق حركة الفلك الثامن حتى ذهب بعضهم إلى أنها بحركته، واختار الآخرون كونها حركات الممثلات بذواتها ، احترازاً عن كونها عطلاً. والتزموا عدم تحركها بحركة الثامن لأن تحريك الحاوي للمحوي ليس بلازم
As for their motions to the succession, among them are the motions of the representative spheres except the moon's representative sphere. They appear at the apogees and perigees and are in accordance with the motion of the eighth sphere, such that some scholars held that they move by its motion, while others chose that they are motions of the representatives by themselves, to avoid them being idle. They committed to their not being moved by the motion of the eighth because the mover of the container for the contained is not necessary.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage discusses the motions of the representative spheres (excluding the moon's) which are observed at the apogees and perigees. These motions align with the motion of the eighth sphere (the sphere of fixed stars). There are two opinions: some say they move because of the eighth sphere, while others say they move by their own nature, to avoid them being idle (without purpose). The latter argue that it is not necessary for the container (the eighth sphere) to move its contents (the inner spheres).

Key Terms
الأفلاك الممثلة
الفلك الثامن
حركات الممثلات بذواتها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All representative spheres' motions are necessarily driven by the eighth sphere.
Correction: Some scholars argue they move by themselves to avoid being idle, using the principle that the container does not necessarily move the contained.

Checkpoint

A) To avoid them being idle
B) Because they follow the eighth sphere
C) Because they are fixed
D) Because the moon moves them

Key Takeaway
The passage highlights two competing explanations for the motion of representative spheres—external causation from the eighth sphere versus internal self-motion—reflecting deeper principles about necessity and purpose in celestial mechanics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see patterns in your life that seem to be caused by external factors, do you ever consider that they might originate from your own self? This lesson forces you to consider self-motion versus external causation. Which view do you lean towards, and why? And does your choice reflect a deeper assumption about agency?
?
The scholars argued that the spheres move themselves to avoid being 'idle'. Where in your life have you assumed passivity—that you are moved by circumstances—when actually you have the capacity for self-motion? What would it mean to adopt the position of self-motion in that area?
?
Are you willing to accept that what appears to be caused by something external might actually be from its own nature, even if it seems counterintuitive? How does this lesson challenge your default assumption about causality in your own life?

Why Astronomers Added Additional Celestial Spheres
Explains why astronomers posited extra spheres due to observed anomalies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why medieval astronomers found it necessary to add extra celestial spheres to explain observed planetary motions.

Core Idea
Observational anomalies forced astronomers to infer extra spheres.

Medieval astronomers used a system of spheres to explain celestial motions. However, when they looked closely at the moon and planets, they found irregularities that could not be explained by the simple model. This led them to propose additional spheres, despite their perplexity about the details. In this passage, al-Sanusi outlines key anomalies that drove these additions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's reasoning come through.
2
Identify the main anomalies
Look for the three specific observational discrepancies mentioned: for the moon, the planets (especially Mercury and Venus), and the inclination of orbital planes.
These are the core evidence for needing extra spheres.
3
Understand the logical necessity
For each anomaly, ask: why does this contradict the simple deferent-epicycle model? The passage explains that certain parameters should align with the deferent's center, but observations show otherwise.
This shows how deductive reasoning from observation leads to model adjustments.
4
Reflect on the role of conjecture
Notice the author's remark that astronomers established these spheres 'by conjecture' (حدس). Consider the methodological point: even with anomalies, the models remained provisional.
This highlights the tentative nature of scientific theories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال هذا ولكنهم وجدوا اختلافات أخر تقتضي زيادة أفلاك تحيروا في كيفياتها، وكمياتها، وأوضاعها وحركاتها وذلك أن كون مركز التدوير متحركاً بحركة الحامل، يقتضي أن يكون تشابه حركته، وتساوي أبعاده ومحاذاة القطر المار بالذروة، والحضيض كلها بالإضافة الى مركز الحامل، وقد وجد في القمر تشابه الحركة حول مركز العالم، ومحاذاة القطر بالنقطة من جانب الحضيض بعدها مركز العالم كبعد ما بين المركزين وفي المتحيرة تشابه الحركة حول نقطة على منتصف ما بين مركز العالم، ومركز المدير في عطارد والحامل في البواقي، وأيضاً مـيـل الماثل عن الممثل شمالي في نصف جنوبي في آخر، فلزم أن يكون مركز التدوير كذلك، لكنهم وجدوه أبداً للزهرة شمالياً، ولعطارد جنوبياً. يعني أنهم، وإن أثبتوا بحكم الحدس هذه الأفلاك والحركات، لكنهم وجدوا في القمر والخمسة المتحيرة اختلافات أخر تورث إشكالات على ما أثبتوا.
He said: But they found other differences requiring additional spheres, and they were perplexed about their qualities, quantities, positions, and motions. And that is because the fact that the center of the epicycle moves with the motion of the deferent necessitates that its motion, the equality of its distances, and the alignment of the diameter passing through the apogee and perigee are all with respect to the center of the deferent. And in the moon they found similarity of motion around the center of the world, and alignment of the diameter with the point on the side of the perigee where its distance from the center of the world equals the distance between the two centers. And in the planets they found similarity of motion around a point halfway between the center of the world and the center of the director in Mercury and the deferent in the others. Also, the inclination of the inclined plane from the equinoctial plane is northern in half and southern in another, so it necessitated that the center of the epicycle be likewise, but they found it always northern for Venus and southern for Mercury. Meaning that, even though they established these spheres and motions by conjecture, they found in the moon and the five planets other differences that cause problems for what they established.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage discusses the complexities found by astronomers that required additional celestial spheres. It begins by noting that astronomers discovered irregularities that compelled them to add more spheres, leaving them puzzled about their qualities, quantities, positions, and motions. The core issue is that if the epicycle's center moves with the deferent's motion, then similarity of motion, equal distances, and alignment of the apogee-perigee diameter should all be relative to the deferent's center. However, in the moon, they observed similar motion around the earth's center and alignment with a point on the perigee side such that the distance from earth's center equals the distance between the two centers (i.e., the earth is not at the center of the moon's orbit). Among the planets, they found similar motion around a point midway between the earth and the center of the equant (or deferent). Additionally, the inclination of the orbital plane varies: northern for Venus, southern for Mercury. These observational discrepancies forced them to posit additional spheres to save the phenomena. The author remarks that despite establishing these spheres through conjecture, the anomalies remain problematic.

Key Terms
فلك التدوير
الحامل
الذروة
الحضيض
الماثل
الممثل
الحدس
مركز العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Medieval astronomers believed spheres were physical objects like glass orbs.
Correction: Many medieval astronomers, including those referenced here, considered spheres as mathematical models to save the phenomena, not necessarily physical realities.

Checkpoint

A) Because they found the existing spheres were too few.
B) Because observations showed irregularities that could not be explained by the simple system.
C) Because the Quran required more spheres.
D) Because the moon's orbit is a perfect circle.

Key Takeaway
Observational discrepancies in the moon and planets led astronomers to add extra spheres to their celestial models, even though these additions raised new questions.

What one unresolved question about your Creator's creation are you avoiding facing?

The author notes that the extra spheres were established 'by conjecture' (الحدس), yet these conjectures were grounded in careful observation. The Geometric Ideal: Equal Angles, Arcs, and Alignment
Geometric conditions from uniform circular motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four geometric conditions that should hold if a celestial sphere's center moves uniformly on a circle: equal angles in equal times, equal arcs in equal times, constant distance from the center, and constant alignment of a fixed diameter with a fixed point.

Core Idea
Uniform circular motion implies equal angles, equal arcs, and constant alignment.

This lesson introduces the ideal geometric framework that astronomers expected to govern planetary motions. Before examining actual observations, we must grasp what would logically follow from simple uniform motion on a circle. This sets the stage for understanding the problems of alignment and similarity discussed in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse every detail. Then read the translation. Let the author's description of the geometric scenario sink in.
The passage uses letters to label points in a diagram. Try to visualize the circle and the moving sphere.
2
Identify the four consequences
The passage lists four consequences of uniform circular motion: equal angles, equal arcs, constant distance, and alignment of a diameter. Find each in the text.
Each consequence is introduced by the phrase 'ويلزم أيضاً' or similar.
3
Understand the meaning of 'alignment' and 'similarity'
Note that 'alignment' (المحاذاة) refers to the fixed diameter remaining pointed towards a fixed point. 'Similarity' (تشابه الحركة) refers to equal angles and arcs generated in equal times.
These terms are key to understanding the problems in the next lesson.
4
Reflect on why this is an ideal
Ask yourself: Why would these conditions be important for the Ptolemaic model? They are what one would expect if the epicycle's center moves uniformly on its deferent.
This ideal will be compared to observations in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أفلاك والحركات مثل إشكال المحاذاة وإشكال تشابه الحركة، وإشكال عرض السفليين فمنهم من تحير، ومنهم من تصدى لحل البعض مع الاعتراف بالخلل فيه وادعى صاحب التحفة حل الجميع وجه إشكال المحاذاة والتشابه، أنه إذا تحرك مركز كرة كنقطة (أ) التي هي مركز كرة (ب) ج) على محيط دائرة كدائرة (اي (ء) وكانت تلك الحركة بسيطة حدثت عند مركز ذلك المحيط وهو (ر) في أزمنة متساوية زوايا متساوية كزوايا (ازء زه)، ويتبع ذلك تساوي قسي المحيط في تلك الأزمنة كقسي (اءءه) ويلزم أيضاً أن تكون أبعاد مركز الكرة المفروضة عن نقطة (ر) أيضاً متساوية في جميع الأوضاع كخطوط (زازعزه) إذ كل منها نصف قطر دائرة (اءه) ويلزم أيضاً أن يكون قطر (ب) ج) من الكرة المفروضة أبداً محاذياً لنقطة ( ز ) حتى إذا صار مركز الكرة من (ا) إلى (ء) كان القطر مثل (ج ط)، وإذا صار إلى (ه) كان مثل (ك) (ل) فمركز التدوير إذا كان متحركا على محيط حامله الخارج المركز كما قدروه لزم أن تكون الأمور الثلاثة بالنسبة إلى مركز الخارج لكنها بالأرصاد المعتبرة لم توجد كذلك، بل وجد في القمر تشابه حركة مركز التدوير أعني إحداث الزوايا المتساوية في الأزمنة المتساوية حول مركز العالم، ومحاذاة القطر المار بالذروة والحضيض لنقطة من جانب الحضيض لا الأوج على ما وقع في المواقف سهواً بعدها عن مركز العالم كبعد ما بين مركز العالم ومركز الخارج المركز أعني نقطة تتوسط مركز العالم كبعد ما بين مركز الخارج فاتجه الإشكالان، ووجد في عطارد تشابه الحركة حول نقطة على منتصف ما بين مركز العالم ومركز المدير وفي الزهرة والعلوية على منتصف ما بين مركز العالم ومركز الحامل فاتجه على كل اشكال وأما محاذاة القطر في المتحيرة، وإن لم يكن لمركز الحامل، لكنها لما كانت للنقطة التي بحسبها تتشابه الحركة لم يتجه
From the spheres and motions such as the problem of alignment (المحاذاة) and the problem of similarity of motion (تشابه الحركة), and the problem of the latitude of the lower planets (عرض السفليين). Some were perplexed, and some undertook to solve part of it while admitting a flaw in it, and the author of al-Tuhfa claimed to have solved all. The aspect of the problem of alignment and similarity is that if the center of a sphere, like point (A) which is the center of sphere (B C), moves on the circumference of a circle, like circle (D) (i.e., (ء)), and that motion is simple, then at the center of that circumference, which is (R), equal angles occur in equal times, like angles (AZ Z H). This is followed by equality of arcs of the circumference in those times, like arcs (A H H). It also necessarily follows that the distances of the assumed sphere's center from point (R) are equal in all positions, like lines (Z A Z' Z H), since each is a radius of circle (A H). It also necessarily follows that the diameter (B C) of the assumed sphere is always aligned with point (Z), so that when the sphere's center goes from (A) to (H), the diameter is like (J T), and when it goes to (W), it is like (K L). So if the center of the epicycle (مركز التدوير) moves on the circumference of its deferent (حامل), which is the eccentric (خارج المركز), as they supposed, then the three things would necessarily hold relative to the center of the eccentric. But by reliable observations they were not found to be so. Rather, in the Moon there was found similarity of the epicycle's motion, i.e., generating equal angles in equal times around the center of the world, and alignment of the diameter passing through the apogee and perigee towards a point on the side of the perigee, not the apogee—as accidentally occurred in al-Mawaqif—its distances from the world's center being like the distance between the world's center and the center of the eccentric, i.e., the point that bisects the distance between the world's center and the center of the eccentric. So the two problems arose. In Mercury there was found similarity of motion around a point at the midpoint between the world's center and the center of the director (المدير), and in Venus and the upper planets around the midpoint between the world's center and the center of the deferent, so every problem arose. As for the alignment of the diameter in the planets [other than the Moon], even though it was not for the center of the deferent, yet since it was for the point with respect to which the motion is similar, it did not arise.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of two astronomical problems (إشكالات) in the Ptolemaic model: the problem of alignment (المحاذاة) and the problem of similarity of motion (تشابه الحركة). It also mentions a third problem, the latitude of the lower planets, which will be discussed later. The author notes that scholars reacted differently: some were perplexed, others attempted partial solutions while admitting flaws, and one claimed to have solved all. He then explains the geometry underlying the expected behavior: if a sphere's center moves uniformly on a circle, then from the center of that circle, equal angles and arcs occur in equal times, distances from that center remain equal, and a fixed diameter of the sphere aligns constantly with a fixed point. In the Ptolemaic system, these conditions should hold for the epicycle's center moving on its eccentric deferent, but observations show they do not. For the Moon, similarity of motion and alignment occur but with respect to a different point (the center of the world and a point offset from the eccentric center), so the problems arise. For Mercury, similarity occurs around a midpoint between the world's center and the director's center; for Venus and upper planets, around a midpoint between the world's center and the deferent's center—so every planet has its own problem. However, the alignment problem does not arise for these because it is defined relative to the point of similarity, not the deferent's center.

Key Terms
إشكال المحاذاة
إشكال تشابه الحركة
مركز التدوير
خارج المركز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The geometric conditions described are exactly what is observed in real planetary motions.
Correction: These conditions are idealizations based on uniform circular motion. Actual observations show deviations, leading to the problems of alignment and similarity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the alignment condition require?
A) The sphere's diameter remains pointed towards a fixed point.
B) The sphere's diameter remains parallel to a line.
C) The sphere's diameter rotates uniformly.
D) The sphere's diameter aligns with the center of the world.

Key Takeaway
Uniform circular motion of a sphere's center implies four geometric properties: equal angles, equal arcs, constant distance from the center, and alignment of a fixed diameter with a fixed point.

Observed Discrepancies in Planetary Motions
Observed discrepancies and arising problems.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how actual observations of the Moon, Mercury, Venus, and upper planets deviate from the ideal geometric conditions, giving rise to the problems of alignment and similarity.

Core Idea
Observations show that planets do not follow the ideal geometric conditions, creating the problems that Ptolemaic astronomers had to solve.

In the previous lesson, we learned the ideal conditions that should hold if an epicycle's center moves uniformly on its deferent. Now, we examine actual astronomical observations. These observations reveal that the Moon, Mercury, Venus, and the upper planets each deviate from the ideal in specific ways, giving rise to the two problems of alignment and similarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the 'three things'
The passage begins by restating the three conditions that should hold relative to the eccentric center. Find them.
These are equal angles, equal arcs, and alignment.
2
Compare the ideal with the Moon's observed motion
The text says that for the Moon, similarity occurs around the world's center, not the eccentric center. Alignment also occurs relative to a different point. Note the two problems that arise.
This is the key deviation.
3
Examine the cases of Mercury, Venus, and upper planets
For Mercury, similarity is around a midpoint between world center and director center. For Venus and upper planets, around a midpoint between world center and deferent center.
Note that for these, alignment does not become a problem.
4
Understand why alignment problem does not arise for some planets
The passage explains that for planets other than the Moon, alignment is defined relative to the point of similarity, so it does not create an additional problem.
This resolves why only the Moon has both problems.

من أفلاك والحركات مثل إشكال المحاذاة وإشكال تشابه الحركة، وإشكال عرض السفليين فمنهم من تحير، ومنهم من تصدى لحل البعض مع الاعتراف بالخلل فيه وادعى صاحب التحفة حل الجميع وجه إشكال المحاذاة والتشابه، أنه إذا تحرك مركز كرة كنقطة (أ) التي هي مركز كرة (ب) ج) على محيط دائرة كدائرة (اي (ء) وكانت تلك الحركة بسيطة حدثت عند مركز ذلك المحيط وهو (ر) في أزمنة متساوية زوايا متساوية كزوايا (ازء زه)، ويتبع ذلك تساوي قسي المحيط في تلك الأزمنة كقسي (اءءه) ويلزم أيضاً أن تكون أبعاد مركز الكرة المفروضة عن نقطة (ر) أيضاً متساوية في جميع الأوضاع كخطوط (زازعزه) إذ كل منها نصف قطر دائرة (اءه) ويلزم أيضاً أن يكون قطر (ب) ج) من الكرة المفروضة أبداً محاذياً لنقطة ( ز ) حتى إذا صار مركز الكرة من (ا) إلى (ء) كان القطر مثل (ج ط)، وإذا صار إلى (ه) كان مثل (ك) (ل) فمركز التدوير إذا كان متحركا على محيط حامله الخارج المركز كما قدروه لزم أن تكون الأمور الثلاثة بالنسبة إلى مركز الخارج لكنها بالأرصاد المعتبرة لم توجد كذلك، بل وجد في القمر تشابه حركة مركز التدوير أعني إحداث الزوايا المتساوية في الأزمنة المتساوية حول مركز العالم، ومحاذاة القطر المار بالذروة والحضيض لنقطة من جانب الحضيض لا الأوج على ما وقع في المواقف سهواً بعدها عن مركز العالم كبعد ما بين مركز العالم ومركز الخارج المركز أعني نقطة تتوسط مركز العالم كبعد ما بين مركز الخارج فاتجه الإشكالان، ووجد في عطارد تشابه الحركة حول نقطة على منتصف ما بين مركز العالم ومركز المدير وفي الزهرة والعلوية على منتصف ما بين مركز العالم ومركز الحامل فاتجه على كل اشكال وأما محاذاة القطر في المتحيرة، وإن لم يكن لمركز الحامل، لكنها لما كانت للنقطة التي بحسبها تتشابه الحركة لم يتجه
From the spheres and motions such as the problem of alignment (المحاذاة) and the problem of similarity of motion (تشابه الحركة), and the problem of the latitude of the lower planets (عرض السفليين). Some were perplexed, and some undertook to solve part of it while admitting a flaw in it, and the author of al-Tuhfa claimed to have solved all. The aspect of the problem of alignment and similarity is that if the center of a sphere, like point (A) which is the center of sphere (B C), moves on the circumference of a circle, like circle (D) (i.e., (ء)), and that motion is simple, then at the center of that circumference, which is (R), equal angles occur in equal times, like angles (AZ Z H). This is followed by equality of arcs of the circumference in those times, like arcs (A H H). It also necessarily follows that the distances of the assumed sphere's center from point (R) are equal in all positions, like lines (Z A Z' Z H), since each is a radius of circle (A H). It also necessarily follows that the diameter (B C) of the assumed sphere is always aligned with point (Z), so that when the sphere's center goes from (A) to (H), the diameter is like (J T), and when it goes to (W), it is like (K L). So if the center of the epicycle (مركز التدوير) moves on the circumference of its deferent (حامل), which is the eccentric (خارج المركز), as they supposed, then the three things would necessarily hold relative to the center of the eccentric. As for the alignment of the diameter in the planets [other than the Moon], even though it was not for the center of the deferent, yet since it was for the point with respect to which the motion is similar, it did not arise.

The Latitude Problem of Venus and Mercury
Taftazani explains the latitude anomaly of Venus and Mercury and the missing cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the anomaly in the Ptolemaic model regarding the latitudes of Venus and Mercury and why it requires an unexplained mover.

Core Idea
The lower planets break the expected latitude alternation, revealing a gap in Ptolemaic causation.

Taftazani presents a third problem with the Ptolemaic model: the observed latitudes of Venus and Mercury do not match the expected pattern from the orbital geometry. While theory predicts alternating northern and southern positions, observations show each planet remains on one side. This passage highlights the need for an additional mechanism that Ptolemy did not explain.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Taftazani uses technical terms like منطقة الماثل and منطقة الممثل.
2
Identify the expected vs. observed behavior
The geometry predicts that the epicycle center should alternate between northern and southern latitudes. However, observations show Venus always at node or north, Mercury at node or south. Mark this contrast.
The text says: لكنهم وجدوه للزهرة دائماً، إما على العقدة، وإما في الشمال.
3
Understand the proposed mechanism and its missing cause
The text describes a coincidence and separation of the two planes that would cause the latitude to swap, but notes that a mover (محرك) is necessary yet not mentioned. Ask yourself: why is this a problem for the model?
The missing mover means the model is incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عرض ها هنا أشكال اختلاف المحاذاة كما في القمر، ووجه اشكال السفليين، أن تقاطع منطقتي الماثل والممثل تقتضي أن تكون أحد نصفيه شمالياً من الممثل والآخر جنوبياً، ولما كان مركز التدوير في سطح المائل لزم أن يكون كذلك، لكنهم وجدوه للزهرة دائماً، إما على العقدة، وإما في الشمال، ولعطارد دائماً، إما على العقدة، وإما في الجنوب، بناء على أن انطباق المنطقتين، وانفصالهما بحيث إذا انتهت حركة مركز تدوير الزهرة من الرأس إلى الذنب، وجاز أن ينتقل إلى جانب الجنوب صار نصف ماثله الشمالي جنوبياً، والجنوبي شمالياً، فكان انتقاله إلى الشمالي، وهكذا أبداً، وعطارد بالعكس، ولا بد لهذا الانطباق والانفصال من محرك ولم يذكروه .
Here arises a problem of difference in alignment as in the Moon, and the aspect of the problem of the lower planets is that the intersection of the planes of the deferent and the inclined [plane] requires that one of its halves be northern relative to the deferent and the other southern. And since the center of the epicycle is on the inclined plane, it must be so. But they found it for Venus always either at the node or in the north, and for Mercury always either at the node or in the south, based on the fact that the two planes coincide and separate such that when the motion of the epicycle center of Venus from the head to the tail ends, and it may transfer to the southern side, its northern half [of the deferent?] becomes southern, and the southern becomes northern, so its transfer was to the northern, and so on always. And Mercury is the opposite. And this coincidence and separation must have a mover, but they did not mention it.

Commentary
This passage presents the third problem, the latitude (عرض) of the lower planets (Venus and Mercury). The author explains that according to the Ptolemaic model, the intersection of the plane of the deferent (الماثل) and the plane of the inclined (الممثل) should cause the epicycle's center to alternate between northern and southern latitudes. However, observations show that Venus is always either at the node or in the north, and Mercury is always either at the node or in the south. The text describes a hypothesized mechanism where the two planes coincide and separate, causing the latitude to switch, but no cause for this mechanism is provided. The author concludes that a mover (محرك) is necessary but was not mentioned, thus the model is incomplete.

Variation of Day and Night with Latitude and Solar Position
Describes how day length varies with latitude and solar declination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the length of day and night varies with latitude and the sun's position in the zodiac, as described by the author to illustrate cosmic order.

Core Idea
The regular variation of day and night demonstrates cosmic order and divine wisdom.

This passage from a theological work sets out the astronomical principles governing the length of day and night. It explains why days are longer in summer and shorter in winter, and how this differs with latitude. Understanding this regularity is a step towards appreciating the order in creation that points to a wise Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own description come through.
The passage is dense with astronomical terminology; the translation will clarify.
2
Identify the two main variables
Notice that the author uses latitude (عرض) and the sun's position in the zodiac (being in northern or southern signs) as the key factors determining day length.
3
Observe the pattern with latitude
The author states that the difference between night and day increases with latitude. Look for the explanation involving visible and hidden poles.
This is a cause-and-effect relationship.
4
Trace the solstice progression
Follow the description of day increasing up to one solstice and decreasing to the other. This shows the cyclical nature.
The solstices are referred to as 'رأس المنقلب'.
5
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why the author includes this detailed astronomical account in a theological work. It serves as evidence of order and wisdom in creation.
This connects to the broader argument for a wise Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في جنوب المعدل، كانت القسي الظاهرة أعظم في العرض الجنوبي، وأصغر في الشمالي، فعند كون الشمس في البروج الشمالية كان النهار أقصر في العرض الشمالي، وأطول في الجنوبي، وعند كونها في البروج الجنوبية كان الأمر بالعكس، وكلما كان عرض البلد أكثر كان مقدار التفاوت بين الليل والنهار أكثر لازدياد ارتفاع القطب الظاهر والمدارات التي تليه، وازدياد فضل قسيها الظاهرة على الخفية وازدياد انحطاط القطب الخفي، والمدارات التي عنده، فيزداد فضل قسيها الخفية على الظاهرة، ويكون تزايد النهار، وتناقص الليل إلى رأس المنقلب الذي يلي القطب الظاهر، وتناقص النهار، وتزايد الليل إلى رأس المنقلب الآخر، ويكون نهار كل جزء مساوياً لليل نظيره، وبالعكس كنهار أول السرطان لليل أول الجدي وبالعكس.
South of the equator, the visible arcs are greater in the southern latitude and smaller in the northern. Thus, when the sun is in the northern signs, the day is shorter in the northern latitude and longer in the southern; and when it is in the southern signs, the opposite occurs. The more the latitude of a country is, the more the amount of difference between night and day, due to the increase in altitude of the visible pole and the circles adjacent to it, and the increase in the excess of its visible arcs over the hidden ones, and the increase in depression of the hidden pole and the circles near it, so the excess of its hidden arcs over the visible ones increases. The day increases and night decreases up to the solstitial point next to the visible pole, and the day decreases and night increases up to the other solstitial point. The day of each part equals the night of its counterpart, and vice versa, like the day of the first of Cancer for the night of the first of Capricorn, and vice versa.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a scientific description of the variation in day length depending on latitude and the sun's position in the zodiac. The author explains that south of the equator, the visible arcs of the celestial sphere are larger in southern latitudes and smaller in northern latitudes. Consequently, when the sun is in northern signs (summer in the north), days are shorter in the north and longer in the south; the opposite occurs when the sun is in southern signs (winter in the north). The author then notes that the difference between night and day increases with latitude, due to the increasing altitude of the visible pole and the arcs around it, and the increasing depression of the hidden pole. This leads to a description of the progression from one solstice to another, where day and night lengthen or shorten correspondingly. Finally, the author states that the day of any part equals the night of its counterpart, giving the example of the first day of Cancer (summer solstice in the north) and the first day of Capricorn (winter solstice). This precise astronomical regularity serves as a background for the theological argument that follows, demonstrating order in creation that points to a wise creator.
